class=\"linked-articles__btn event_read-more-articles\" data-event-action=\"Next Article\"><b>Next</b> article in issue<span\n\t\t\t\t\tclass=\"fa-icon fa-icon--right\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\"\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\txmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg\" viewBox=\"0 0 192 512\"><path\n\t\t\t\t\td=\"M0 384.662V127.338c0-17.818 21.543-26.741 34.142-14.142l128.662 128.662c7.81 7.81 7.81 20.474 0 28.284L34.142 398.804C21.543 411.404 0 402.48 0 384.662z\"></path></svg></span></a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2021ApJ...916...50F\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2021ApJ...916...50F\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\"><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s1\" name=\"apjac0257s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Strong emission-line ratios have emerged as powerful diagnostics to understand the physical conditions within distant (redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a01) galaxies, particularly the metallicity, pressure, and ionization state of the gas and the amount of dust (e.g., Kewley &amp; Dopita <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib39\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib39\">2002</a>; Pettini &amp; Pagel <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib62\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib62\">2004</a>; Rigby et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib65\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib65\">2011</a>; Nakajima &amp; Ouchi <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib50\">2014</a>; Steidel et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib72\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib72\">2014</a>, among many others). Most observational studies that have used these diagnostics to characterize distant galaxies have, by necessity, used the integrated light of entire galaxies to measure them. However, a spatially integrated measurement is unlikely to fairly represent all regions within a galaxy. Distant galaxies show kiloparsec-scale structures, called \"giant clumps\" (e.g., Elmegreen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib19\">2005</a>; Guo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib26\">2012</a>), though recent observational and theoretical results suggest that far smaller spatial scales\u2014tens of parsecs rather than kiloparsecs\u2014are important for star formation in the distant universe (Mandelker et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib49\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib49\">2013</a>; Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib35\">2017</a>). A spatially integrated spectrum may well be dominated by the spectrum of one bright giant clump (or a single complex of smaller clumps), if it has extreme line ratios compared to the rest of the galaxy, particularly at bluer rest wavelengths. For instance, Girard et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib22\">2018</a>) find that about 40% of the star formation, as indicated by H<em>\u03b1</em>, lies in just three clumps in a lensed galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.6. Moving beyond a bulk measurement of galaxy spectra to truly understand the internal physics of these sources requires spectroscopic studies with high spatial resolution.</p><p>Surveys using integral field units (IFUs) have characterized how strong line ratios vary spatially in nearby galaxies. Metallicity gradients, for instance, have been observed in the local universe (e.g., Belfiore et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib3\">2017</a>; Poetrodjojo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib63\">2018</a>), at low redshifts (e.g., 0.1\u00a0\u2264\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2264\u00a00.8 in Carton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib7\">2018</a>), and at moderate redshifts (e.g., lensed sources at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.49 and 2 in Yuan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib83\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib83\">2011</a> and Jones et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib36\">2010</a>, respectively). Meanwhile, Poetrodjojo et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib63\">2018</a>) have investigated, but did not find strong evidence of, radial gradients in ionization parameter at low redshifts, though other studies such as Ellison et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib18\">2018</a>) have found evidence of radial gradients in star formation rate (SFR) surface densities, and Dopita et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib13\">2014</a>) find correlations between SFR and ionization parameter.</p><p>While spatial variation of strong line diagnostics at subgalactic scales is well established in low-redshift galaxies, it is not yet clear how these diagnostics vary spatially in more distant galaxies, which have systematically more extreme physical conditions (Kewley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib42\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib42\">2015</a>; Holden et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib29\">2016</a>; Onodera et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib55\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib55\">2016</a>) and far more disturbed morphologies in which giant clumpy structures are far more prevalent (Elmegreen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib19\">2005</a>; Shibuya et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib70\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib70\">2016</a>). Furthermore, the star formation histories of clumps in such young and disordered objects are likely very different from those of star-forming regions in the local universe. For example, the star formation history of a single star-forming clump at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u20133 is more likely to be accurately described by a single stellar population than structures in older and more morphologically mature galaxies like the Milky Way would be since there has not been as much time for secondary bursts or mixing with older stellar populations from within the same galaxy or from mergers. It is therefore reasonable to suspect that in addition to more extreme physical conditions, higher-redshift objects might also have more extreme variations in those conditions.</p><p>Additionally, the spatial variation of these diagnostics likely has important consequences for galaxy evolution and cosmology. For example, the strong line ratio O32 has been found to correlate with Lyman continuum (LyC) leakage (Nakajima et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib51\">2013</a>; Izotov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib30\">2018</a>), likely due to its sensitivity to ionization parameter. But it is unclear whether this is a galaxy-wide phenomenon or a smaller, more localized one. Izotov et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib30\">2018</a>) and Nakajima et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib51\">2013</a>) identify LyC leakage in the integrated light of their target galaxies, for example, but in a strongly lensed source, Rivera-Thorsen et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib66\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib66\">2019</a>) find LyC leakage from only a single clump. Understanding the details of processes like this will be critical to understanding how the universe became reionized.</p><p>Even with large space telescopes like the Hubble Space Telescope (HST) and the upcoming James Webb Space Telescope (JWST), diffraction limits prevent the study of spatial scales below \u223c500\u00a0pc in distant field galaxies (and while the HST WFC3 UVIS channel's point-spread function (PSF) allows for \u223c500 pc spatial resolution at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02, the IR channel is actually limited to the kiloparsec scale). The exceptions are galaxies that have been highly magnified by gravitational lensing, thereby providing access to otherwise unresolvable physical structures within the source, which can be critical to making certain measurements and inferences.</p><p>For example, while IFU spectroscopy has enabled the measurement of metallicity gradients in large samples of unlensed field galaxies at cosmic noon, these studies are limited to roughly kiloparsec-scale spatial resolutions, and low spatial resolution is known to effectively flatten measured gradients (Yuan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib82\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib82\">2013</a>). The KMOS<sup>3D</sup> team, for instance, attempted to measure metallicity gradients in a sample of 419 objects and found statistically significant evidence (3<em>\u03c3</em>) of gradients in only 15 objects (Wuyts et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib80\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib80\">2016</a>). Whether the rest are flat or simply shallow is a question for higher spatial resolution spectroscopy. Wang et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib76\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib76\">2020</a>) went a step further, using a sample of 76 lensed galaxies, and found 15 of them to have gradients with at least 2<em>\u03c3</em> significance at the resolution of a few hundred parsecs (median magnification of only 2.69, and only four sources with magnifications greater than 10). Even higher magnifications (\u223c10 or more) have enabled the study of SFRs (Whitaker et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib78\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib78\">2014</a>), metallicity gradients (Jones et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib36\">2010</a>; Patricio et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib56\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib56\">2019</a>), and rotation curves (Tiley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib75\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib75\">2019</a>) with resolutions as fine as tens of parsecs to a couple of hundred parsecs, as well as measurements of the sizes of individual star-forming regions at the 30 pc scale (Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib34\">2017</a>). However, the sample of such extremely highly magnified galaxies where spatially resolved spectroscopy covering important diagnostic emission lines in the rest-frame optical (e.g., being able to observe both [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727+3729 at the blue end and H<em>\u03b1</em> at the red end) is possible on scales of only tens of parsecs is still quite small.</p><p>In this paper, we use HST grism spectroscopy from GO14230 (PI: Rigby) to measure the standard suite of rest-frame optical strong emission lines, from [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729 to [S <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>6716, 6733, in two strongly lensed (average magnification of about 10 and 50) galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.4 selected from the Sloan Giant Arcs Survey (SGAS; Bayliss et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib2\">2011</a>; Sharon et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib68\">2020</a>). We map the spatial variation of the diagnostic line ratios, which are sensitive to dust, metallicity, and ionization parameter (a measure of the ratio of ionizing photons to hydrogen nuclei). In particular, we examine the following diagnostics:</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">Balmer decrement\u00a0\u2261\u00a0H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em>.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R23\u00a0\u2261\u00a0([O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>4959, 5007 + [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729)/H<em>\u03b2</em>.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">O32\u00a0\u2261\u00a0[O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>4959, 5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">4.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">Ne3O2\u00a0\u2261\u00a0 [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3869/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> ] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729.</div></li></ul><p>The Balmer decrement is sensitive to dust, while the others are sensitive to metallicity and ionization parameter. R23 is primarily sensitive to metallicity but has a secondary dependence on ionization parameter, while O32 and Ne3O2 are primarily sensitive to ionization parameter with a secondary dependence on metallicity.</p><p>We quantify the spatial variation in these strong line ratios and examine the corresponding variation in inferred physical characteristics of the nebular gas.</p><p>We also examine whether the spatially integrated spectra of these two galaxies tell the whole story of\u2014or even accurately summarize\u2014the physical properties of the nebular gas in the multiple distinct physical regions that are probed at lensing-boosted spatial resolution. Each of these objects provides an opportunity to see, directly, how much we miss by using integrated spectra. SDSS\u00a0J2340+2947, at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.42, is lensed in such a way that there are four complete images of the source galaxy, each of which contains three distinct spatial regions from which we can obtain spectra. The other source, SDSS\u00a0J1723+3411 at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.33, exists in a lensing configuration such that there are two partial (but nearly complete) images of the source combining to form a giant arc, as well as two other magnified complete images and a central, demagnified complete image. The northernmost complete image is well enough separated from the brightest cluster galaxy (BCG) and intracluster light that its spectrum can also be extracted robustly from the HST grism spectroscopy for comparison.</p><p>This paper is organized as follows. Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s2\">2</a> describes the experimental design and sample selection. Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s3\">3</a> describes the broadband imaging, HST spectroscopy, and ground-based spectroscopy that we have obtained to carry out this experiment. Details of emission-line fitting are given in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s4\">4</a>. Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5\">5</a> discusses the observed spatial variation of the strong emission-line ratios, explores the implied corresponding variation in physical parameters, and compares the implied measurements for spatially integrated versus spatially resolved spectra. Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s6\">6</a> discusses the implications of such spatial variation in emission-line ratios for studying galaxy evolution and the epoch of reionization and explores considerations for future observational and theoretical work.</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s2\" name=\"apjac0257s2\">2.\u00a0Experimental Design and Sample Selection</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>This study requires technically demanding spectroscopy that fulfills three criteria. First, the highest possible spatial resolution is needed; this demands that the targets be gravitationally lensed, and further that they be observed either from space or with ground-based adaptive optics systems. Second, the spectra must have complete wavelength coverage from rest-frame 3727\u00a0\u00c5 (to cover the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet) to 6730\u00a0\u00c5 (to cover the [S <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet). Third, the spectra must have excellent relative fluxing over that entire wavelength range, in order to use diagnostic line ratios. Together, these criteria drive the experiment to use the WFC3-IR grisms on board HST. Of currently available spectrographs, only the WFC3-IR grisms provide high spatial resolution, excellent flux calibration, and uninterrupted wavelength coverage over this range.</p><p>Used together, the G102 and G141 WFC3-IR grisms can cover the desired range of rest wavelength for galaxies in a narrow redshift range 1.15 \u2272 <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.58. We therefore selected galaxies in this redshift range from SGAS. We required that the galaxies appear bright enough to obtain high-quality grism spectra, are highly magnified, and have lensing configurations that are amenable to modeling. Only two targets emerged from this selection: SDSS\u00a0J1723+3411 (hereafter SGAS J1723) with <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.3294\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0002 (Kubo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib43\">2010</a>), and SDSS\u00a0J2340+2947 (hereafter SGAS J2340) with <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.420\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.003. SGAS J1723 is one of the brightest lensed sources in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS; York et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib81\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib81\">2000</a>) footprint and has been reported in several independent searches for lensed galaxies within those data (Kubo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib43\">2010</a>; Wen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib77\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib77\">2011</a>; Stark et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib71\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib71\">2013</a>). SGAS J2340 has not been previously reported. This lensing system was found as part of the SGAS visual examination of SDSS lines of sight with putative clusters or groups of galaxies and confirmed as a lens using <em>gri</em> imaging from the 2.5 m Nordic Optical Telescope's MOSCA instrument on UT 2012 September 16, with the lensed source then spectroscopically confirmed using the same telescope's ALFOSC spectrograph on UT 2013 September 1.</p><p>To support the HST grism spectroscopy, we obtained ground-based spectroscopy from large ground-based telescopes. We obtained rest-frame ultraviolet (observed-frame optical) spectra with the Echellette Spectrograph and Imager (ESI; Sheinis et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib69\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib69\">2002</a>) on the Keck\u00a0II telescope. We obtained rest-frame optical spectra of [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] and H<em>\u03b1</em> with the Gemini Near-InfraRed Spectrograph (GNIRS; Elias et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib16\">2006</a>) on the Gemini-North telescope. These instruments provide much higher spectral resolution than the WFC3-IR grisms, but much lower spatial resolution since they are seeing limited. Additionally, broadband imaging from HST and Spitzer was leveraged for the creation of lens models, interpretation of source morphologies, and the estimation of stellar masses of each source.</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s3\" name=\"apjac0257s3\">3.\u00a0Observations, Data, and Data Reduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Here we describe the observations, data, and data reduction for the spectra from Keck ESI, Gemini GNIRS, and the HST grisms, as well as the broadband imaging from HST and Spitzer. All wavelengths are listed in vacuum. Source coordinates and redshifts are listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t1\">1</a> for ease of reference.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjac0257t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 1.</b>\u00a0The Positions and Redshifts of the Targets in This Paper</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257t1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t1_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=2LhgpIBhUkSF6SNfG3eQvULeg90%3D\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 1\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead><tr valign=\"top\"><th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Source</th><th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">R.A. Redshifts and uncertainties are for the lensed source galaxies and were determined by the GNIRS spectroscopy reported in this paper (Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-5\">5.5</a>).</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t1_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=2LhgpIBhUkSF6SNfG3eQvULeg90%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s3-1\" name=\"apjac0257s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Broadband HST Imaging</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We acquired broadband imaging for SGAS J2340 and SGAS J1723 using the Wide Field Camera 3 (WFC3) on board HST, as needed to construct a lens model and do contamination modeling and wavelength calibrations for the grism data.</p><p>SGAS J1723 was observed in six bands with HST WFC3: F160W, F140W, F110W, and F105W in the IR channel, and F775W and F390W in the UVIS channel. Imaging in the F160W and F110W bands was conducted as part of HST GO13003 (PI: Gladders) on 2013 March 14 for 1112 s each. Imaging with the UVIS channel in the F775W and F390W bands was conducted as part of the same program, with total integration times of 2380 and 2368 s, respectively. Imaging in the F140W and F105W bands was conducted as part of HST GO14230 (PI: Rigby) in 2016 January and July alongside the grism observations, for a total integration of 923 s per band.</p><p>SGAS J2340 was observed in four bands with HST WFC3: F140W and F105W in the IR channel, paired with the grism observations, and F814W and F390W in the UVIS channel, all from program GO14230 (PI: Rigby). In the IR channel, SGAS J2340 was observed with the F105W filter for 973 s and with F140W for 1635 s; in the UVIS channel, it was observed with the F814W filter for 2504 s and with F390W for 2600 s.</p><p>For all HST broadband imaging, a 4-point dither pattern was used. To reduce the imaging data, the images were aligned using the Drizzlepac<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjac0257fn1\">\n                  13\n               </a></sup>\n                routine <em>tweakreg</em> and drizzled to a common reference grid with a pixel scale of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />03 pixel<sup>\u20131</sup> using <em>astrodrizzle</em> with a \"drop size\" (final_pixfrac) of 0.8. Three-color images of both SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=3JW%2Fsm4AvLBqOUVSyLENY65rQyc%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=3JW%2Fsm4AvLBqOUVSyLENY65rQyc%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Left: three-color HST image (R: F160W; G: F775W; B: F390W) of SDSS\u00a0J1723+3411, with critical curves plotted in red and labels of each image and region in white. Images 1 and 2 are incomplete images, with regions A\u2013D appearing once in each half of the arc. Images 3, 4, and 5 are complete images. Image 3 is separated enough from the BCG that grism spectra could be extracted with minimal contamination. Right: three-color HST image (R: F140W; G: F814W; B: F390W) of SDSS\u00a0J2340+2947, with critical curves plotted in red and labels for each region in white. There are four complete images with three distinct physical regions that could be extracted from the grism spectroscopy in each. Once again, the numbering in the labels denotes individual images of the lensed source, and the lettering denotes corresponding subregions. Lens models are described in Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-1\">5.1</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f1\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=3JW%2Fsm4AvLBqOUVSyLENY65rQyc%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f1\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f1_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=jOkFYYeE%2B8OGY5C5RrZnk200RAs%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s3-2\" name=\"apjac0257s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Broadband Spitzer Imaging</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Data from the IRAC instrument of the Spitzer Space Telescope, acquired during the post-cryogenic \"warm mission,\" were obtained through program 90232 (for SGAS J1723; PI J. Rigby) and program 12001 (for SGAS J2340; PI J. Rigby). The individual frame times were 30 s; the total per-pixel integration times were 30 minutes in IRAC channel 1 (3.6 <em>\u03bc</em>m) and 10 minutes in IRAC channel 2 (4.5 <em>\u03bc</em>m). We processed the Spitzer IRAC Ch1 and Ch2 images as follows. At a high level, we followed the general guidance of the IRAC Cookbook for reducing the COSMOS medium-deep data, though with more stringent (3<em>\u03c3</em>) outlier rejection, and with residual bias correction.</p><p>In more detail, we downloaded the \"corrected basic calibrated data products\" (cBCDs) from the Spitzer archive. These cBCDs are the exposure-level data that have been processed by the IRAC pipeline to remove instrumental signatures and artifacts and to calibrate into physical units. We applied the warm mission column pull-down correction (bandcor_warm by Matt Ashby) to mitigate column artifacts from bright sources.</p><p>For deep integrations, residual bias pattern noise and persistence can dominate over the background. To mitigate these effects, we constructed images of the residual bias, also known as a \"delta dark frame.\" For each channel in each observation, we created a residual bias correction from all the cBCDs, by detecting and masking sources in each image, adjusting the DC level of each image so that the modes had the same value, and then taking the median with 3<em>\u03c3</em> outlier rejection. The relevant median image was then subtracted from every cBCD image in that channel and that observation.</p><p>For each target and each filter, we combined the individual images into a mosaic as follows using the MOPEX command-line tools (Makovoz &amp; Marleau <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib48\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib48\">2005</a>). We used its overlap correct tool to add an additive correction for each residual-bias\u2013corrected cBCD image to bring it to a common sky background level. We then combined these images into a mosaic using the mosaic tool, using the drizzle algorithm with a pixel fraction of 0.6, and 3<em>\u03c3</em> outlier rejection using the box outlier rejection method.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s3-3\" name=\"apjac0257s3-3\">3.3.\u00a0Keck ESI Spectroscopy: 4000\u201310000 \u00c5 Observed</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Both galaxies were observed with the ESI spectrograph on the Keck\u00a0II telescope in echellette mode with a 1'' slit on the nights of 2016 August 27 and 28 UT. Observing time was obtained through the Australian National University. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f2\">2</a> shows how slits were oriented for observations of SGAS J2340 and SGAS J1723. SGAS J1723 was observed each night, with a slit placed along the length of the arc, for 3600 s the first night and 3800 s the second night. For SGAS J2340, each of the four complete images were observed each night with the following strategy. Images 1 and 2 were observed simultaneously, for 3800 s on the first night and 3600 s on the second night. Images 3 and 4 were observed simultaneously, for 3600 s on each night. Light from all three spatial subregions of SGAS J2340 was captured by the slit.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=c1RamDElHzqztn9hQhIy0FLBQT0%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=c1RamDElHzqztn9hQhIy0FLBQT0%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Finder charts to show spectroscopic slit positions for the lensed galaxies SDSS\u00a0J1723+3411 (panel (a)) and SDSS\u00a0J2340+2947 (panel (b)). The background image for each is HST WFC3-IR F105W. The long rectangles show the Keck ESI pointings (with a 1 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 20'' long slit). For SGAS J1723, this paper uses ESI spectroscopy from the slit that runs along the length of the arc. For SGAS J2340, the ESI slits each captured a pair of images of the lensed galaxy: 1 and 2 in one slit, 3 and 4 in the other. Line fluxes, equivalent widths, and diagnostic ratios measured from the ESI spectra and reported in this paper come from the sum of these spectra. The ESI slits were positioned by offsetting from the BCG, which is also marked. The red rectangles show the Gemini GNIRS pointing for each target, with a 0.3 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 7'' slit. North and east are shown with a compass. Image IDs (1\u20134, corresponding to the labels in Figure <a href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a>) are also shown for reference.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f2\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=c1RamDElHzqztn9hQhIy0FLBQT0%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f2\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f2_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=HPPWiI29F%2Fs2bndx07gB%2FKlJaJ4%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We reduced the Keck ESI spectra following the same procedure as Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>). For SGAS J2340, we extracted the spectrum of each image individually. Line ratios are measured from the sum of the four images' spectra. The Keck/ESI data provide spatially integrated spectroscopy at <em>R</em>\u00a0\u2248\u00a04000.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s3-4\" name=\"apjac0257s3-4\">3.4.\u00a0Gemini GNIRS Spectroscopy: \u223c14600\u201316600 \u00c5 Observed</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Gemini GNIRS observations of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 were obtained through the Gemini Fast Turnaround mode in program GN-2016B-FT-11 (PI Rigby). Observations were conducted on UT 2016 September 7. Observations used the short camera, cross-dispersing prism (\"SXD\" mode), 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />3 slit, and 111\u00a0line mm<sup>\u20131</sup> grating. Data were obtained as A\u2013B nods. For SGAS J1723 the central wavelength was set to 1.529 <em>\u03bc</em>m; for SGAS J2340 it was set to 1.588 <em>\u03bc</em>m, covering wavelength ranges of 1.46\u20131.60 <em>\u03bc</em>m and 1.52\u20131.66 <em>\u03bc</em>m, respectively. These ranges were chosen to capture the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet and H<em>\u03b1</em>. [S <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] also falls in this window, but it was not detected. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f2\">2</a> shows where the GNIRS slit was positioned for SGAS J2340. A similar figure for SGAS J1723 is available in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>). For SGAS J1723 the GNIRS slit primarily captured light from the brightest region in the southern part of the arc, region A1. For SGAS J2340 the GNIRS slit primarily captured light from the central region, \"B.\" For SGAS J1723, the cumulative integration time (discarding one exposure with data quality issues) was 2970 s. For SGAS J2340, 12 integrations of 270 s duration were obtained, for a total integration time of 3240 s.</p><p>The GNIRS spectra were reduced in IRAF using the GNIRS pipeline, which does sky subtraction by differencing A\u2013B pairs. From each A\u2013B pair, spectra of the A and B images were extracted using a 7-pixel-wide boxcar. We combined the individual spectra by calculating the mean spectrum and the error in the mean. Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>) discuss special care that had to be taken with the reduction for SGAS J1723, due to the fact that the grating shifted position during the observations.</p><p>It is worth noting that although the resolution of GNIRS in this setup is typically <em>R</em>\u00a0=\u00a05900, for SGAS J1723 the grating slipped during observations (see Rigby et al.<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\"> 2021</a> for a more thorough discussion of this) and the achieved spectral resolution was only about 1900.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s3-5\" name=\"apjac0257s3-5\">3.5.\u00a0HST Grism Spectroscopy: 8500\u201316500 \u00c5 Observed</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Spectroscopy for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 was conducted using the HST WFC3/IR G141 and G102 grisms alongside the direct imaging from program GO14230 described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s3-1\">3.1</a>.</p><p>At the redshift of these arcs, <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.4, these grism observations cover the wavelength range from just blueward of [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729 to just redward of H<em>\u03b1</em>. Each target was observed twice with each grism, using two different roll angles to facilitate the modeling of contamination from cluster galaxies. For SGAS J1723, observations in each grism were performed for 5112 s at one roll angle and 4812 s at the other. SGAS J2340 was observed with a similar strategy except that the exposure times were 7518 s for both roll angles with the G141 grism and 5012 and 5112 s for the two roll angles with the G102 grism.</p><p>The HST grism spectra were reduced with the software package Grizli<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjac0257fn2\">\n                  14\n               </a></sup>\n                (Brammer <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib5\">2018</a>). We followed the standard Grizli reduction pipeline steps, with a notable extra step of <tt>GALFIT</tt> (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib61\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib61\">2010</a>) modeling to account for the contaminating light of the cluster galaxies. This extra step is described in detail in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>) and was performed on the grism data for both targets. In brief, bright sources whose spectra significantly overlap with the spectra of these arcs were modeled with GALFIT. Grism spectral contamination models were then created for each one based on the modeled light profiles without considering contamination from the rest of the field (which was modeled separately). The contamination models based on the GALFIT model profiles were then recombined with those of the rest of the field and further refined simultaneously to create the final contamination model.</p><p>In this paper, we separately extract the HST grism spectra of physically distinct regions within each of the lensed galaxies, guided by the source-plane morphologies described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-2\">5.2</a>. (This is in contrast to the approach of Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>), which considers only the spatially integrated 1D spectrum of the giant arc of SGAS J1723.) These regions are labeled with letters in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a>. The 1D spectrum of each individual subregion was constructed by summing over the relevant rows in the 2D grism spectrum and then stacking the spectra of the multiple lensed images of that region. When the lensing geometry and orientation relative to the dispersion axis of the grisms allow for low morphological broadening and little to no spectral contamination from other pieces of the arcs, spectra from both roll angles are also summed.</p><p>For SGAS J1723 we separately extract the HST grism spectra for the three clumps (A, B, D) and a diffuse component of the giant arc (C), each of which are imaged twice (A1, A2; B1, B2; etc.), and additionally extract the spectrum of the northern complete image (image 3).</p><p>For SGAS J2340 we separately extract the HST grism spectra for the following physically distinct regions. For region A, we extract a spectrum from three of the four lensed images at one roll and one of the images at the other roll. For region B, we extract a spectrum from three images at one roll and two images at the other. For region C, we extract a spectrum from two images at each roll (one image at both rolls, and two other images at one roll each). These decisions were guided by the quality of the grism contamination models and the orientation of each image relative to the dispersion axis. The spectra of each region were stacked over the multiple images and rolls. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t2\">2</a> summarizes which spectra were included in each of these stacks. For visual reference, Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f3\">3</a> shows the 2D grism spectra (before contamination modeling), with the low-contamination spectra used in this paper marked by yellow rectangles and the higher-contamination spectra not used for this paper marked with dashed black rectangles.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f3_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=wR4rzqCTpGXIHK0ffZp419i7s2M%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f3_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=wR4rzqCTpGXIHK0ffZp419i7s2M%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0The 2D grism spectra of SGAS J2340 before contamination modeling for both grisms and both rolls. Solid yellow rectangles mark spectra that were successfully extracted with low contamination from traces of other objects' spectra and are used in this work, corresponding with Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t2\">2</a>. The bottom two panels are spectra from roll 2, again with G102 on the left (panel (c)) and G141 on the right (panel (d)). Spectra are dispersed in each panel such that bluer wavelengths are on the left and redder wavelengths are on the right. Note that spectra of C1 and C4 overlap slightly for the first roll angle and contaminate each other. They are similar in brightness, so their mutual contamination is problematic for extraction of spatially resolved spectra. However, the overlap is only partial, and they are so faint relative to regions A and B that their mutual contamination negligibly influences the spatially integrated spectra of images 1 and 4.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f3\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn1.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=m%2FvjAhut04NTmRM3CtiTzsAQ2uM%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span> values measured by Green et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib24\">2015</a>).<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjac0257fn3\">\n                  15\n               </a></sup>\n               \n            </p></div></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s4\" name=\"apjac0257s4\">4.\u00a0Data Analysis Methods</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjac0257s4-1\" name=\"apjac0257s4-1\">4.1.\u00a0Fitting Emission Lines in the Keck ESI Spectra</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We fit emission lines in the ESI spectra using the continuum and emission-line fitting routines described in Acharyya et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib1\">2019</a>). Briefly, we fit one Gaussian profile per emission line, simultaneously for a group of neighboring lines. A neighbor is defined as emission lines whose centroids are within \u00b15 spectral resolution elements of the line in question. The emission-line fluxes and equivalent widths for SGAS J1723 are reported in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>), and those for SGAS J2340 are reported in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t5\">5</a>.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s4-2\" name=\"apjac0257s4-2\">4.2.\u00a0Fitting Emission Lines in the Gemini GNIRS Spectra</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The purpose of the GNIRS spectroscopy, as it pertains to this paper, was to measure the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]/H<em>\u03b1</em> ratio. We fit the spectra with Gaussians using MPFIT, as described in Wuyts et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib79\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib79\">2014</a>). The uncertainty spectrum was used as weights in the fitting. The central wavelengths of all lines were set using the rest wavelength from NIST and the measured H<em>\u03b1</em> redshift. The widths of all lines were forced to vary in lockstep. The flux ratio of the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet was locked at the value from Storey &amp; Zeippen (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib73\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib73\">2000</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s4-3\" name=\"apjac0257s4-3\">4.3.\u00a0Fitting Emission Lines in the HST Grism Spectra</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Line fluxes were measured from the stacked spectra using the custom fitting technique described in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>), with a few minor changes to compensate for the lower signal-to-noise ratios (S/Ns) of the spectra of individual regions, compared to the spatially integrated spectrum of the giant arc studied in that paper. Two iterations of the fitting algorithm were run on each spectrum. The first iteration solves for the redshift, the morphological line broadening (a nuisance parameter), and the line fluxes and uncertainties. The second iteration fixes the redshift and morphological broadening parameter determined in the first iteration and then allows for small variations in the observed wavelength of each emission feature; this is motivated by known uncertainties in the wavelength solutions of HST grism spectra. The second iteration typically resulted in better overall spectral fits. However, for a few low-S/N spectra (the integrated spectra of images 1, 2, and 3 of SGAS J2340 from the G102 grism), the second iteration resulted in poorer fits; for those spectra we report only the line fluxes measured from the first iteration.</p><p>At the low spectral resolution of the WFC3/IR grisms, the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet is unrecoverably blended with H<em>\u03b1</em>. Therefore, we set the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet ratio to its theoretical value. We also set the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>5008, 4959 ratio and [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3870, 3869 ratio to theirs. Values for each of these ratios are taken from Storey &amp; Zeippen (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib73\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib73\">2000</a>). Furthermore, we set the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]/H<em>\u03b1</em> ratio to the value measured from the spatially integrated Gemini GNIRS spectrum of each galaxy (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-5\">5.5</a>). Similarly, the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 flux ratio was set to the value measured from the Keck ESI spectra (Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-4\">5.4</a>). These values were used for all physical regions of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 despite coming from the integrated spectrum.</p></div></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s5\" name=\"apjac0257s5\">5.\u00a0Results</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-1\" name=\"apjac0257s5-1\">5.1.\u00a0Lens Models</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We used the strong-lensing evidence, i.e., identification of multiply imaged lensed galaxies, in order to compute strong-lensing models for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. The lensing analysis of SGAS J1723 was published in Sharon et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib68\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib68\">2020</a>) as part of the SGAS-HST program. We describe here the lensing analysis of SGAS J2340. However, we note that the lensing analysis of both clusters follows the same procedure.</p><p>We identified two strongly lensed galaxies in this field. Source\u00a01, the topic of this paper, has four complete images around the core of the cluster. The images are resolved and show identical morphology and color variation. We used the central positions of four distinct morphological features in each image, as well as the spectroscopic redshift of the source galaxy, <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.42, as lensing constraints. Source\u00a02 appears as three images of a faint galaxy, 6<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />44 northwest of the BCG. Its redshift is unknown and was used as a free parameter in the lens modeling process. Constraints are tabulated in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t3\">3</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjac0257t3\" class=\"boxout rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u00a0</td><td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small><p>\n                     <strong>Note.</strong> IDs correspond to labels in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a>. Region B has been broken up into two components (labeled with lowercase a and b) for modeling. B1a is the northern half of region B in image 1. B2a is the southern half of region B in image 1. IDs beginning with \"11\" correspond to a second source not studied in this paper.</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t3_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=s2aN9yht7NdfwbzHMQoN%2BqJ0io4%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The lens model was computed using the publicly available software <tt>Lenstool</tt> (Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib37\">2007</a>). <tt>Lenstool</tt> uses a Bayesian approach to explore the parameter space and identify the best-fit model, as the set of parameters that minimize the scatter between the predicted and observed lensed images in the image plane. The lens model results in a parametric 2D description of the lens plane, from which the projected mass density, lensing magnification, and deflection are derived.</p><p>The lens was modeled as a linear combination of parameterized mass halos. Each halo was assumed to be a pseudo-isothermal elliptical mass distribution (PIEMD, or dPIE; El\u00edasd\u00f3ttir et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib17\">2007</a>), with the following parameters: position <em>x</em>, <em>y</em>; ellipticity <em>e</em>; position angle <em>\u03b8</em>; core radius <em>r</em><sub><em>c</em>\n               </sub>; truncation radius <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub>; and normalization <em>\u03c3</em><sub>0</sub>. The lens is composed of cluster-scale halos and galaxy-scale halos. The latter were placed at the positions of observed cluster-member galaxies, identified using the red sequence technique (Gladders &amp; Yee <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib23\">2000</a>) in the F814W\u2013F105W color\u2013magnitude space. The position, ellipticity, and position angle of the galaxy halos were fixed to their observed values as measured with Source Extractor (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib4\">1996</a>). The other parameters are scaled to the luminosity, following Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib46\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib46\">2005</a>). All the parameters of cluster-scale halos were left free, except for <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub>, which is beyond the range that can be constrained by the lensing evidence. It was fixed to 1500 kpc.</p><p>We find that the lens is best described by two cluster/group-scale halos, combined with galaxy-scale halos. The statistical uncertainties were derived by computing the lensing outputs from sets of parameters drawn from steps in the MCMC chain. Magnifications and the corresponding uncertainties are tabulated for both this source and SGAS J1723 in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>. The relatively small number of lensed galaxies in this field limited the number of constraints available for lens modeling, resulting in more uncertain models and relatively larger statistical uncertainties in magnification than for SGAS J1723.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjac0257t4\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 4.</b>\u00a0Magnifications, Magnitudes, <strong>Note.</strong> Columns (1) and (2) denote the source and the image or subregion. Column (3) contains the magnifications of each region and each complete image of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. Uncertainties are reported as the 68% level, e.g., for SGAS J1723 region A1, 68% of models that produce magnifications below 16.6 produce magnifications above 15.0 and 68% of models that produce magnifications larger than 16.6 produce magnifications below 17.1. Columns (4)\u2013(10) contain the magnitudes of each region or complete image obtained from simple aperture photometry in each of the available HST filters using apertures that trace the segmentation map, with minor adjustments to divide up the individual regions as described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-3\">5.3</a>. For the purposes of planning future observations, the observed H<em>\u03b2</em> flux is included for each component in Column (11), with its uncertainty in Column (12) (in units of 10<sup>\u221217</sup> erg s<sup>\u22121</sup> cm<sup>\u22122</sup>). Rather than reporting line fluxes based on fits of individual, often low-S/N spectra, we report values measured from the stacked spectra of all images of each region, scaled based on the number of roll angles and the flux ratios from the broadband imaging. The flux ratios used for scaling here are determined from the stacks of the imaging data in the UVIS channel because the higher spatial resolution allows better separation of the subregions, while the flux ratios are consistent regardless of wavelength.</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t4_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t4_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=0RaWXPRIQdhiGSrBgBP0NJIACwQ%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-2\" name=\"apjac0257s5-2\">5.2.\u00a0Source Morphologies</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The lens models enable a reconstruction of the source-plane morphology, which informs our extraction and summation of the HST grism data.</p><p>The giant arc in SGAS J1723 is a merging pair of images of a single source galaxy. Each of these images is nearly complete. As Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a> shows, six large clumps are apparent in the broadband imaging; these are two images of each of the three physically distinct clumps (A, B, and D). An additional region, labeled C, appears to correspond to either a diffuse component or multiple spatially unresolved clumps. In addition to the giant arc in SGAS J1723, there are two complete but less magnified images of the lensed galaxy (images 3 and 4) and a demagnified central image (5). The grism spectra of images 4 and 5 are badly contaminated by the BCG; we were, however, able to extract the spectrum of the northern complete image (3).</p><p>There are four lensed images of the source galaxy SGAS J2340. Each features a bright central region (B) and two fainter clumps near the edges (A and C). All of these regions, for both sources, are labeled in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a> and correspond to the regions from which the spectra described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s3-5\">3.5</a> were extracted. Because the dither pattern of the HST imaging observations allows us to oversample the PSF, our final drizzled data products are able to resolve region B into two subcomponents for the purposes of lens modeling. However, drizzling spectra produce correlated noise that can mimic emission or absorption features, so the Grizli algorithm uses interlacing instead. For the interlacing, we use the native pixel scale, which is about four times coarser than the pixel scale we used in reducing the drizzled direct images. As a result, the spectra of the two subcomponents of region B are spatially blended.</p><p>To summarize, for SGAS J1723 we extract spectra of four physically distinct regions, as well as one complete image; for SGAS J2340 we extract spectra of three regions and also create a stacked composite spectrum of the complete images.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-3\" name=\"apjac0257s5-3\">5.3.\u00a0Photometry from the HST Images</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Broadband magnitudes for SGAS J2340 and the giant arc in SGAS J1723 were determined using a <tt>GALFIT</tt> decomposition of each source galaxy. Using these integrated magnitudes, magnitudes measured from the Spitzer data, the magnifications in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>, and the stellar population synthesis (SPS) parameter inference code <tt>Prospector</tt> (Leja et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib44\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib44\">2017</a>), we estimated stellar masses of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn31.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=v8PmDi%2Fqzj%2BVlqkmZKdb6qO2TFA%3D\" alt=\"${9.67}_{-4.4}^{+9.0}\\times {10}^{8}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{9.67}_{-4.4}^{+9.0}\\times {10}^{8}</script></span></span> \n               <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn32.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=T5Q3u%2Fnw%2BBV0cg%2F3zDG3bKMi3WM%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> for the source in SGAS J2340 and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn33.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Q4CvQdC92hD02CEpV0AlgpJIkqc%3D\" alt=\"${5.95}_{-1.86}^{+2.2}\\times {10}^{8}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{5.95}_{-1.86}^{+2.2}\\times {10}^{8}</script></span></span> \n               <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn34.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=ubybvrfki6hxWocuEG58StzVnqM%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> for SGAS J1723. Details of these measurements and the process used to infer the stellar masses are included in the <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257app1\">Appendix</a>. For the purposes of planning future observations, approximate apparent magnitudes (uncorrected for lensing magnification) of each individual region in these images based on photometry from custom apertures are included, along with the magnifications, in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>. These apertures were designed to match the segmentation map for each object except that individual spatially resolved regions inside each source were separated by a single straight line, parallel to the spectral dispersion direction in one of the roll angles for each source. Where the critical curve crosses the giant arc in SGAS J1723, the dividing line between images D1 and D2 was drawn to not cross the best-fit critical curve in order to provide a more stable magnification estimate. We also include the estimated H<em>\u03b2</em> flux for each region determined by correcting the H<em>\u03b2</em> flux from the stacked spectrum using the observed broadband flux ratios of the various images of each region.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-4\" name=\"apjac0257s5-4\">5.4.\u00a0Keck ESI Results</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Fluxes for emission lines measured from the ESI spectra for SGAS J1723 are listed in Table 1 of Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>), and those for SGAS J2340 are listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t5\">5</a> of this paper. Spectra and line fits are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f4\">4</a> for SGAS J2340. The equivalent figure is available in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>), Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f6\">6</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f4_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=kPVpqp4bN6j59LkA%2BsRg%2BvPfRgU%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f4_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=kPVpqp4bN6j59LkA%2BsRg%2BvPfRgU%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Emission lines detected in the Keck/ESI spectrum of SGAS J2340. Spectra are shown as black steps. Brown vertical lines and labels indicate the best-fit central wavelengths of lines detected at the 3<em>\u03c3</em> level or greater. Brown curves show the fits of individual components, while green curves show the sum of separate fitted spectral components. Undetected lines are marked in black, and the dashed vertical blue lines mark the region on which the fitting routine was run.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span
