align=\"center\">21.8</td><td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">4.80</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small><p>\n                     <strong>Note.</strong> The reported numbers are measured from the summed spectra of the four images. Images 2, 3, and 4 are 0.91, 1.09, and 0.40 times as bright, respectively, as image 1. Parameters flux<sub>obs</sub> and <em>\u03b4</em> flux<sub>obs</sub> denote the observed flux and uncertainty, respectively. <em>W</em><sub>r, fit</sub> and <em>\u03b4 W</em><sub>r, fit</sub> denote the rest-frame equivalent width measured and the corresponding uncertainty in \u00c5, respectively, with negative values indicating emission (rather than absorption) lines. For cases of nondetection (i.e., &lt;3<em>\u03c3</em> detection), the 3<em>\u03c3</em> upper limits on equivalent widths and fluxes are quoted. For ease of planning potential future observations, these values are not dereddened.</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t5_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t5_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=SfLFPtOZUro3mRyLcyGclUQxjuU%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>For SGAS J1723, the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 flux ratio was measured as 0.71\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01. For SGAS J2340, the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 flux ratio was measured as 0.82\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.01.</p><p>From these ratios, we can infer pressures (Kewley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">2019a</a>). For SGAS J1723 this pressure is about log(<em>P</em>/<em>k</em>)\u00a0=\u00a06.0, while for SGAS J2340 it is log(<em>P</em>/<em>k</em>)\u00a0=\u00a06.5. These values are measured from spatially integrated spectra, but because the HST grisms do not spectrally resolve this doublet, we adopt these values for all subregions in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-8-2\">5.8.2</a>.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-5\" name=\"apjac0257s5-5\">5.5.\u00a0GNIRS Gemini Results</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>For SGAS J1723, results from the Gemini GNIRS spectrum were presented in Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>). The redshift was measured as <em>z</em>(H<em>\u03b1</em>)\u00a0=\u00a01.3293\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0002. The [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>6586/H<em>\u03b1</em> flux ratio was measured to be 0.062\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.011.</p><p>For SGAS J2340, we measure the redshift of H<em>\u03b1</em> as <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.42151\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.00002. The [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>6586/H<em>\u03b1</em> flux ratio is measured to be 0.084\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03 (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f5\">5</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f5_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=%2Ba3SDHBRlLIBSbE4281ujwn4ONo%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f5_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=%2Ba3SDHBRlLIBSbE4281ujwn4ONo%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0H<em>\u03b1</em> and the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet in the Gemini GNIRS spectrum of SGAS J2340. Black steps show the summed 1D spectrum; red steps show the uncertainty spectrum, and the blue curve shows the best fit.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f5\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f5_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=%2Ba3SDHBRlLIBSbE4281ujwn4ONo%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f5\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f5_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=QmYcR3xEOgXHogfEENhOnHY64tY%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>These values are spatially integrated for SGAS J2340 and come from clump A1 in SGAS J1723. Note that the uncertainty on the redshift of SGAS J1723 is a factor of 10 larger than that of SGAS J2340. This is because of the slippage of the GNIRS grating during observations of SGAS J1723 that we described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s3-4\">3.4</a> and Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-6\" name=\"apjac0257s5-6\">5.6.\u00a0Line Flux Measurements from the HST Grism Spectra</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>An example of a reduced 2D grism spectrum for a single image of SGAS J2340 and the 1D extraction and line fitting for each subregion is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f6\">6</a>. Line fluxes for the stacks of each region in SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 are listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t6\">6</a> without corrections for magnification or the number of roll angles or the image multiplicity. To find the flux for a specific single image, one can simply scale by the H<em>\u03b2</em> fluxes in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>. Similarly, to correct for magnification, one can use the magnifications tabulated in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>. The fully reduced 1D spectra are made available in a machine-readable format on Zenodo:<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"webref\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.4747939\">10.5281/zenodo.4747939</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f6\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f6\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f6_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=LZiRTv7AtmewaaDMfdUMWsNG%2Fgg%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 6.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; align=\"center\">7.47</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small><p>\n                     <strong>Note.</strong> These values are measured from the stacked spectra of multiple images and rolls (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s3-5\">3.5</a> and Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t2\">2</a>) and are not corrected for magnification. To correct to fluxes of single images of a given region, scale by the corresponding H<em>\u03b2</em> flux listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>. To further correct to source-plane fluxes for a given region, magnifications are also listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a>.</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t6_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t6_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=axD1D0qRysnI0YICwtpwknrKd8E%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-7\" name=\"apjac0257s5-7\">5.7.\u00a0Spatial Variation of Strong Line Diagnostics</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We investigate the spatial variation of several strong line diagnostics sensitive to dust, ionization parameter, metallicity, and SFR. Of these, only the H<em>\u03b1</em> flux, an SFR indicator, is sensitive to the magnification due to gravitational lensing. The others, because they are flux ratios rather than fluxes, are invariant under lensing. Here, we describe the degree of variation seen in observables\u2014line fluxes and ratios. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-8\">5.8</a> we explore how these variations correspond to variation in physical parameters, namely, metallicity and ionization parameter.</p><h4 id=\"apjac0257s5-7-1\" name=\"apjac0257s5-7-1\">5.7.1.\u00a0Ratios Sensitive to Reddening: H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> and H<em>\u03b2</em>/H<em>\u03b3</em>\n               </h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We use Balmer decrements to estimate the reddening at each region within these two sources assuming case B recombination and <em>R</em><sub><em>v</em>\n                  </sub>\u00a0=\u00a03.1 using IRAF's <em>deredden</em>, which is based on the empirical extinction function from Cardelli et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib6\">1989</a>) in this wavelength range. For SGAS J1723, H<em>\u03b1</em> falls in G141, H<em>\u03b3</em> falls in G102, and H<em>\u03b2</em> is covered by both grisms. We find that H<em>\u03b2</em> fluxes measured in G102 are more consistent from roll to roll than those measured from G141; we attribute this to H<em>\u03b2</em> falling at an observed wavelength where the sensitivity of the G141 grism is rapidly declining. For SGAS J2340, H<em>\u03b1</em> and H<em>\u03b2</em> are both captured by the G141 grism, while H<em>\u03b3</em> is captured by G102. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f7\">7</a> shows the measured H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> flux ratios from which we infer <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn40.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=egCfiHEgUQu7V9IKP3TMlFkiuXg%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span> values.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f7\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f7\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f7_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Uk7ml2gOXgjRB9UNnTf0MwOFgAs%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 7.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 7.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f7_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Uk7ml2gOXgjRB9UNnTf0MwOFgAs%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 7.</strong>\u00a0The H<em>\u03b1</em>-to-H<em>\u03b2</em> ratios in SGAS J1723 (left) and SGAS J2340 (right). The latter shows significant spatial variation, with region C being uniquely low. The spatial variation in SGAS J1723 is less pronounced, though the difference between region B and region C is suggestive (but not statistically significant). The red bands in each plot show the spatially integrated values measured from the stack of the complete images of SGAS J2340 and from the northern complete image of SGAS J1723; the widths of the bands correspond to the uncertainties. In blue bands we show the values measured from the integrated spectrum of the giant arc in SGAS J1723. For reference, several values of <span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn41.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=MxNFM07AUnM18uw%2BJ0%2BVuuRDzzk%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span> for case B recombination and <em>R</em><sub><em>v</em>\n                        </sub>\u00a0=\u00a03.1 are shown by gray dashed lines. While all of the H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> values are in general agreement for SGAS J1723, it is clear that the value inferred from the integrated spectrum of SGAS J2340 is not representative of the reddening of region C, while the contribution of region C also pulls the reddening of the complete image down relative to regions A and B. This is discussed in Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s6-1\">6.1</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f7\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f7_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Uk7ml2gOXgjRB9UNnTf0MwOFgAs%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f7\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f7_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=X0sH7i4S81S2p3f9V4RHVS6Iyqg%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>SGAS J1723 does not appear to be substantially reddened at any location. Region C is consistent with an <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn42.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=bTeLNgZiWWvLmM8ido1mT7J1VXg%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span> of zero, though the 1<em>\u03c3</em> measurement uncertainties in the H<em>\u03b1</em> and H<em>\u03b2</em> lines allow <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn43.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=9uewRwZcgCAokg9KcXxpuHGAH1U%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span> to be as high as 0.07. The region with the most reddening is region B, with <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn44.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Iuo4H0tmXe3zxfL7LG51Mu9lyYQ%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span>\u00a0=\u00a00.10\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05. Regions A and D fall in between these values, with reddenings of 0.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05 and 0.04\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09, respectively, although, like region C, they are both consistent with zero. There is little evidence of spatial variation in reddening in SGAS J1723 except that region B may be slightly more reddened than the other regions, as it is the only region inconsistent with zero reddening at about the 2<em>\u03c3</em> level.</p><p>SGAS J2340 shows signs of strong variation in the Balmer line ratios. Regions A and B are more reddened than any of the regions in SGAS J1723, having <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn45.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=ajuEddgqh3gs3xOfbayPrv6VBCY%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span>\u00a0=\u00a00.30\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07 and 0.29\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.06, respectively. Region C, however, is consistent with zero extinction and is more comparable to SGAS J1723 than to the other regions within SGAS J2340. The H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> ratio for region C differs from those of regions A and B by about 2.8<em>\u03c3</em>. Of the three regions within SGAS J2340, region C appears the bluest in broadband imaging, which is consistent with this apparent lower level of reddening but could also be due, for example, to lower metallicities or a younger stellar population.</p><p>In principle, reddening can also be determined using the H<em>\u03b2</em>/H<em>\u03b3</em> ratio. In practice, the smaller wavelength separation relative to H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> and the relative faintness of H<em>\u03b3</em> make it less useful than H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em>. In addition, at the low spectral resolution of the G102 grism, H<em>\u03b3</em> is blended with [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em>4363, which is responsible for the high uncertainties in our quoted H<em>\u03b3</em> flux. We find that, in these spectra, the uncertainties on the H<em>\u03b3</em> flux prevent a meaningful measurement of the reddening via H<em>\u03b2</em>/H<em>\u03b3</em>.</p></div><h4 id=\"apjac0257s5-7-2\" name=\"apjac0257s5-7-2\">5.7.2.\u00a0Ratios Sensitive to Ionization Parameter and Metallicity: O32 and R23</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Several diagnostic strong line ratios are sensitive to both ionization parameter and metallicity to varying degrees. Those observable in the wavelength range in the grism spectroscopy for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 include the following:</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">R23\u00a0\u2261\u00a0([O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>4959, 5007 + [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729)/H<em>\u03b2</em>.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">O32\u00a0\u2261\u00a0[O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>4959, 5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">Ne3O2\u00a0\u2261\u00a0 [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3869/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727, 3729.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">4.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">O3H<em>\u03b2</em>\u00a0\u2261\u00a0[O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/H<em>\u03b2</em>.</div></li></ul><p>It should be noted that some of these ratios have varying definitions in the literature. For example, Levesque &amp; Richardson (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib45\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib45\">2014</a>) use only the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727 line in the definition of Ne3O2, but for this paper we prefer to include the <em>\u03bb</em>3729 line because the blended sum is all that can be measured in spatially resolved regions owing to the low spectral resolution of the HST G102 grism. Similarly, R23 is sometimes defined without the <em>\u03bb</em>3729 line, as in Nakajima et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib51\">2013</a>) (who, incidentally, also choose to parameterize the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]-to-[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] ratio as [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727), though others (e.g., Onodera et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib55\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib55\">2016</a>) include the <em>\u03bb</em>3729 line.</p><p>Of these ratios, O32, Ne3O2, and O3H<em>\u03b2</em> are primarily sensitive to ionization parameter, while R23 is primarily sensitive to metallicity (Henry et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib27\">1994</a>; Kewley &amp; Dopita <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib39\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib39\">2002</a>; Levesque &amp; Richardson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib45\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib45\">2014</a>). O3H<em>\u03b2</em> has a strong dependence on pressure, a quantity for which we do not have spatially resolved indicators, and as a result is a poor indicator of either ionization parameter or metallicity. For this reason, we do not include this diagnostic in our analysis.</p><p>The top row of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f8\">8</a> shows the spatial variation in the diagnostic R23, which is primarily sensitive to metallicity. The values for the regions of SGAS J1723 are somewhat tightly bunched around 8.5; the largest and smallest R23 values\u2014those of regions B and D\u2014disagree at only about the 1.5<em>\u03c3</em> level. By contrast, there is substantial variation across the subregions of SGAS J2340. As we saw with the reddening diagnostics, region C is quite different from the other two regions.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f8\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f8\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f8_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=CUmzTVS6p6KPEehvGX13Wdjj5nQ%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 8.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 8.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f8_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=CUmzTVS6p6KPEehvGX13Wdjj5nQ%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 8.</strong>\u00a0Comparison of the R23, O32, and Ne3O2 values for spatially resolved regions (black points) and the values measured from spatially integrated spectra of either complete images (red) or the SGAS J1723 giant arc (blue). There is a suggestion of spatial variation of R23 and clear variation of O32 in SGAS J1723, as well as significant variation in both R23 and O32 in SGAS J2340. It is also clear from the disagreement between the spatially integrated values and some of the spatially resolved values that integrated spectra do not provide a complete picture of the physical conditions inside galaxies like these (see Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s6-2\">6.2</a>).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f8\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f8_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=CUmzTVS6p6KPEehvGX13Wdjj5nQ%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f8\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f8_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=6RbdpsJj1KZd0a1LtJ3bJg8rTMM%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The middle and bottom rows of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f8\">8</a> show the spatial variation in the diagnostics O32 and Ne302, which are primarily sensitive to ionization parameter. The regions in SGAS J1723 show generally higher O32 than those in SGAS J2340, which suggests that the ionization parameter in SGAS J1723 is systematically higher than in SGAS J2340. Both sources show significant spatial variation in O32. In SGAS J2340, once again, region C stands out, differing from A and B at the 4<em>\u03c3</em> level, while A and B are in close agreement with each other. In SGAS J1723, regions A and B show significantly higher O32 values than regions C and D (at the 5<em>\u03c3</em>\u201310<em>\u03c3</em> level depending on the pair of regions); regions A and B agree with each other within 1.5<em>\u03c3</em>, while there is 2.5<em>\u03c3</em> difference between C and D.</p><p>To summarize, within SGAS J1723, regions A and B have higher O32 values than regions C and D; the same pattern is seen (at lower significance) for the Balmer decrement and R23. Within SGAS J2340, region C displays higher O32, lower R23, and less reddening than the rest of the source.</p><p>As for Ne3O2, the values are slightly higher in SGAS J1723 than in SGAS J2340. We find no evidence of spatial variation of Ne3O2 in either galaxy. Because of the relatively faint [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] line involved and its potential blends with nearby lines, the fractional uncertainties in Ne3O2 are relatively large (up to 25% in SGAS J1723 and larger for SGAS J2340) and greatly exceed any apparent variation in the observed Ne3O2 values.</p></div><h4 id=\"apjac0257s5-7-3\" name=\"apjac0257s5-7-3\">5.7.3.\u00a0Star Formation Rate</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>So far, the values that we have considered are all magnification independent because they rely only on relative fluxes, and gravitational lensing is achromatic. We can also look for variation in the H<em>\u03b1</em> flux, which is a well-known indicator of star formation (Kennicutt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib38\">1998</a>). Unlike the previous values discussed in this paper, though, this quantity is dependent on the magnification of each region. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t4\">4</a> shows the magnifications of each region determined using the lens models discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-1\">5.1</a>.</p><p>For each region in each source, we applied the conversion from H<em>\u03b1</em> to SFR from Kennicutt (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib38\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib38\">1998</a>) using the spatially resolved reddening corrections and magnification corrections. There is significant spatial variation in the SFRs across the two galaxies, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f9\">9</a>. SGAS J2340 is forming stars quite rapidly. The central region (B) exhibits the most star formation, about <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn46.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=BUYE%2FXACF7e5CtYoFpDBeArwnxE%3D\" alt=\"${11.7}_{-1.3}^{+5.9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{11.7}_{-1.3}^{+5.9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>, while the regions near the edges of the source (A and C) are forming about <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn47.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=baRHL3IQCJJvbZecVORoWQ%2BYQZw%3D\" alt=\"${6.2}_{-0.8}^{+3.3}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{6.2}_{-0.8}^{+3.3}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn48.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=DUUuvEPWFtj7WmIhh5sdAE5w4D8%3D\" alt=\"${1.9}_{-0.2}^{+1.0}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{1.9}_{-0.2}^{+1.0}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span> of stars, respectively. This suggests a negative radial gradient in SFRs but also suggests asymmetric star formation. As a check of consistency, the SFR determined by stacking all four complete images is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn49.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=dH7IhmFUgDa4%2F7smJP1sXCHPyNk%3D\" alt=\"${19.3}_{-2.4}^{+10.2}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{19.3}_{-2.4}^{+10.2}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>, which agrees with the sum of the three subregions. Significant uncertainties remain, however, due to the lack of extra constraints for the lens model.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f9\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f9\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f9_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Nf%2B0wRQrmChj%2Bn36argqbdi2bsQ%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 9.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 9.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f9_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Nf%2B0wRQrmChj%2Bn36argqbdi2bsQ%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 9.</strong>\u00a0Variation in SFR from region to region within SGAS J1723 (left) and SGAS J2340 (right). Both show evidence of gradients. SGAS J2340 shows a negative radial gradient, with regions A and C forming stars less rapidly than region B. The SFR of SGAS J1723 is driven primarily by clump A. For reference, the integrated values are also plotted in the same format as Figures <a href=\"#apjac0257f7\">7</a> and <a href=\"#apjac0257f8\">8</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f9\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f9_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Nf%2B0wRQrmChj%2Bn36argqbdi2bsQ%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f9\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f9_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=pqnOWcboQly3bI9hXBzRb6Ld5bM%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>SGAS J1723 is also undergoing rapid star formation driven by two of the three apparent clumps. Regions A and B are forming <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn50.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=z1CmKlOT%2FMbibg9FVZB1iCFCPFw%3D\" alt=\"${5.31}_{-0.36}^{+0.15}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{5.31}_{-0.36}^{+0.15}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn51.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=wvAIr4IpzrR7BlX2skFfLLbRnDo%3D\" alt=\"${1.85}_{-0.12}^{+0.10}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{1.85}_{-0.12}^{+0.10}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> per year, respectively, while regions C and D are forming stars at much lower rates, (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn52.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=4356oTO8zekbuHvqS3RrZf4Q4n8%3D\" alt=\"${0.69}_{-0.05}^{+0.02}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{0.69}_{-0.05}^{+0.02}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span> and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn53.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=cDYM%2Fh5WsD2qpSrqua0tS3yMnQ0%3D\" alt=\"${0.25}_{-0.02}^{+0.01}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{0.25}_{-0.02}^{+0.01}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>). The northern complete image of SGAS J1723 (image 3) appears to have an SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn54.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=KuwEKGDa3A9l15n4CVAeo7Qw36o%3D\" alt=\"${8.19}_{-0.39}^{+0.41}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{8.19}_{-0.39}^{+0.41}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>, almost identical to the sum of these regions (8.10), suggesting that the portion of the galaxy visible in the arc accounts for nearly all of the star formation in SGAS J1723. The low surface brightness diffuse light at the outskirts of SGAS J1723, then, likely contains relatively little star formation (about 0.4 <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn55.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Gk5dtXmnJXfFG1YGPbKU5y%2BMiVc%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>). Since the bright clumps are concentrated near the center of this galaxy, SGAS J1723 may also have a negative gradient in the SFR. However, it is clear that the star formation is patchy and asymmetric, dominated by only two clumps.</p><p>As a check of consistency, the SFR derived from fitting the integrated spectrum of the entire giant arc (i.e., summing the spectrum of the whole arc and fitting the lines) is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn56.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=qRZF2fmNi5vfabxrpDZnsfDc5jI%3D\" alt=\"${7.16}_{-0.20}^{+0.46}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{7.16}_{-0.20}^{+0.46}\\,{M}_{\\odot }\\,{\\mathrm{yr}}^{-1}</script></span></span>, slightly lower than what we measure by summing the measured line fluxes of the individual regions (i.e., extracting spectra for each region and fitting the lines in each), but in agreement within less than 2<em>\u03c3</em>.</p><p>Although SGAS J1723 shows evidence of patchy star formation dominated by two clumps, those clumps are centrally located relative to the faint wisps of light evident at the ends of the arc and in image 3 that extend much farther out from the center of the galaxy. Both sources, therefore, exhibit centrally concentrated star formation. Such excesses have been interpreted as \"inside-out star formation\" in other work (e.g., Nelson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib52\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib52\">2016</a> at similar redshifts, and Ellison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib18\">2018</a> at lower redshifts). However, given that sources like these exhibit star formation that occurs in only a few large clumps, it is unclear how meaningful gradients really are as a way of characterizing the spatial distribution of star formation in patchy, asymmetric galaxies. Perhaps a different metric, like the clumpiness or asymmetry indices or the Gini coefficient of the SFR, would better capture the essence of what is occurring in these types of galaxies. In fact, Curti et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib10\">2020</a>) have recently raised the same issue in the context of metallicity maps, which can also be quite patchy and asymmetric at cosmic noon.</p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s5-8\" name=\"apjac0257s5-8\">5.8.\u00a0Ionization Parameters and Metallicities</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-7-2\">5.7.2</a> we showed that the observable line ratios O32 and R23 vary in a statistically significant way. We now consider whether this can robustly be attributed to real differences in physical parameters. To address this question, we must convert between the observables and physical parameters by referring to photoionization models, in this case MAPPINGS v5.1 models (described in the following subsection), to infer the physical parameters log<em>U</em> (ionization parameter) and <em>Z</em> (metallicity).</p><h4 id=\"apjac0257s5-8-1\" name=\"apjac0257s5-8-1\">5.8.1.\u00a0MAPPINGS Photoionization Model Grids</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We use calibrations from Kewley et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">2019a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib41\">2019b</a>, hereafter <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib41\">K19b</a>, respectively) and Nicholls et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib53\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib53\">2020</a>), which are based on the latest version of results from the MAPPINGS v5.1 photoionization code (see Sutherland &amp; Dopita <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib74\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib74\">1993</a>; Dopita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib14\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib14\">2013</a>). MAPPINGS v5.1 includes the local Milky Way region elemental abundances for 30 elements. Nebular elemental abundances for subsolar metallicities are scaled according to Nicholls et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib54\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib54\">2017</a>). For depletion of nebular elements onto dust grains, the <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib41\">b</a> models adopt the parametric models of Jenkins (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib31\">2009</a>) with an Fe depletion value of \u22121.5 dex. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib41\">b</a> use the atomic data for the 30 elements from the CHIANTI 8 database (Del Zanna et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib11\">2015</a>). The MAPPINGS photoionization code self-consistently computes the ionization structure of the nebulae, accounting for dust absorption, radiation pressure, grain charging, and photoelectric heating of small grains (Groves et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib25\">2004</a>).</p><p>The ionization parameter is the ratio of the local Lyman photon flux (cm<sup>\u22122</sup> s<sup>\u22121</sup>) to the local hydrogen density (cm<sup>\u22123</sup>). This ionization parameter (<em>q</em>), with units of velocity, can be related to a dimension-less ionization parameter (<em>U</em>), which we use in this paper, via the speed of light: <em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>q</em>/<em>c</em>. MAPPINGS defines the ionization parameter at the inner edge of the nebula. The photoionization, excitation, and recombination are calculated in a detailed, self-consistent manner in linear increments of 0.02 step size through the nebula. See L\u00f3pez-S\u00e1nchez et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib47\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib47\">2012</a>) for a full description of the models and geometries.</p><p>The <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib41\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib41\">b</a> calibrations use constant-pressure models with plane-parallel geometry. The interstellar medium pressure values range from log(<em>P</em>/<em>k</em>)\u00a0=\u00a04.0 to log(<em>P</em>/<em>k</em>)\u00a0=\u00a09.0 in increments of 0.5 dex. This pressure corresponds to the total mechanical energy flux imparted on the nebula by the driving stellar source, through contributions from both stellar winds and supernovae. These models compute a detailed temperate and density structure throughout the nebulae, dictated by the metallicity and ionization structure.</p><p>For the purpose of calibrating electron density diagnostics, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a> use constant-density models with electron densities ranging from <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn57.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=mgt%2Bmg5qSezIOnqllx2%2BVhcMbbs%3D\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({n}_{e}/{\\mathrm{cm}}^{3})=0$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({n}_{e}/{\\mathrm{cm}}^{3})=0</script></span></span> to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn58.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=ZnXvNznOswRn2BHtYSS5w04%2Fc8o%3D\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}({n}_{e}/{\\mathrm{cm}}^{3})=5$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}({n}_{e}/{\\mathrm{cm}}^{3})=5</script></span></span> in increments of 0.5 dex. These models compute a temperature structure in the nebula, but unlike the isobaric models, they do not allow for a density structure. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib40\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib40\">K19a</a> point out that the isobaric models are the most realistic given that the sound-crossing timescale in typical nebulae is shorter than the cooling/heating timescale, which allows for the pressure to equalize throughout the nebula.</p><p>The metallicity (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn59.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=UEQEPMSxQrkKn69qsAb0Dp2MLK0%3D\" alt=\"$12+\\mathrm{logO}/{\\rm{H}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">12+\\mathrm{logO}/{\\rm{H}}</script></span></span>) values in the models are constrained by the stellar tracks, which use a coarse grid of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn60.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=GRGTIndpAMgEVTxBL8H%2FzjwsffI%3D\" alt=\"$12+\\mathrm{logO}/{\\rm{H}}=7.63$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">12+\\mathrm{logO}/{\\rm{H}}=7.63</script></span></span>, 8.23, 8.53, 8.93, and 9.23. The models are computed for a range of ionization parameter values from log(<em>q</em>)\u00a0=\u00a06.5 to log(<em>q</em>)\u00a0=\u00a08.5, in increments of 0.25 dex. This range corresponds to log(<em>U</em>)\u00a0\u2243\u00a0\u22124 to log(<em>U</em>)\u00a0\u2243\u00a0\u22122, which covers the typically observed values in H <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> regions (Dopita et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib12\">2000</a>).</p></div><h4 id=\"apjac0257s5-8-2\" name=\"apjac0257s5-8-2\">5.8.2.\u00a0Variation in Ionization Parameter and Metallicity Based on MAPPINGS Models</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The grids used in this section are derived from models where the pressure, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn61.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=qs%2FqTucb1Xw7NUfA1QJKZMSqb1E%3D\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}(P/k)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}(P/k)</script></span></span>, is 6.0 for SGAS J1723 and 6.5 for SGAS J2340, as determined by the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 ratio measured from the ESI spectra of the giant arc (consisting of two nearly complete images) in SGAS J1723 and the sum of the integrated spectra of the complete images of SGAS J2340.</p><p>In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f10\">10</a>, we plot the observed strong line ratios for each region in SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340, as well as for the northern complete image and the giant arc in SGAS J1723 and the stacked spectra of the complete images of SGAS J2340 (three images from one roll, and one image from the other as summarized in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t2\">2</a>) in the O32\u2013R23 and O32\u2013Ne3O2 planes. These points are overlaid on the MAPPINGS grids, from which we infer ionization parameter (log<em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0log<em>q</em>/<em>c</em>) and metallicity (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn62.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Ob6%2Fg%2B9wDTN67o%2FJHom5AKCwHEE%3D\" alt=\"$Z=12+\\mathrm{log}({\\rm{O}}/{\\rm{H}})$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">Z=12+\\mathrm{log}({\\rm{O}}/{\\rm{H}})</script></span></span>). Characteristically, the grids in the O32\u2013R23 plane are double-valued; most of our points fall near the double-valued region or where the grids fold over. Consequently, the interpretation of these inferred parameters will have some amount of degeneracy in that there is both a high-metallicity interpretation and a low-metallicity interpretation. The [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]/H<em>\u03b1</em> flux ratios from GNIRS, approximately 6.2% for region A of SGAS J1723 and 8.4% for region B of SGAS J2340, suggest that these regions do fall almost exactly on the fold. The MAPPINGS models suggest a metallicity near 12+log(O/H)\u00a0\u223c\u00a08.23 for both sources, though it could be as high as 8.6 for SGAS J1723 if it is on the higher-metallicity branch. Similarly, the first-order formula of Pettini &amp; Pagel (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib62\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib62\">2004</a>) returns a metallicity of 8.21\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04 for SGAS J1723 and 8.29\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09 for SGAS J2340. Their third-order formula returns 8.19\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03 for SGAS J1723 and 8.25\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07 for SGAS J2340. Additionally, the ratio of [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>2470 to [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 can be used as a temperature diagnostic, which predicts a temperature of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn63.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=QRBchO5Kj%2Fsa%2BostfP3Cm7tgOME%3D\" alt=\"$11,{384}_{-2759}^{+3067}{\\rm{K}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">11,{384}_{-2759}^{+3067}{\\rm{K}}</script></span></span> for SGAS J2340. This is similar to, but slightly higher than, the 10,300\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0500 and 10,700\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02700 that Rigby et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib84\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib84\">2021</a>) find for SGAS J1723 based on two different [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] diagnostic ratios, and it also suggests a moderate metallicity (Nicholls et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib53\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib53\">2020</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f10\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f10\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f10_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=1BYc92ATyQlaNyOL1jWjSLhlhWY%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 10.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 10.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f10_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=1BYc92ATyQlaNyOL1jWjSLhlhWY%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 10.</strong>\u00a0Spatial variation in physical conditions log<em>U</em> and <em>Z</em> (12 + logO/H) as determined by the O32\u2013R23 and O32\u2013Ne3O2 planes and MAPPINGS models. Red lines indicate curves of constant metallicity, with the color saturation scaling with metallicity. Other colors correspond to curves of constant ionization parameter. Note that the MAPPINGS grid in the O32\u2013R23 plane is double-valued and therefore folds over on itself. Spatial variation in these sources appears to be primarily driven by ionization parameter (and the O32 observable). However, the R23 values of SGAS J2340 also indicate significant variation in metallicity.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f10\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f10_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=1BYc92ATyQlaNyOL1jWjSLhlhWY%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f10\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f10_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=XiGcbzmUJ2Lo6nyL%2B1FRu0bvi9M%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>For SGAS J1723, we see that most of the variation is in O32, not in R23. The model grids indicate that this largely corresponds to variation in the ionization parameter. Regardless of which metallicity branch is assumed, the log<em>U</em> in each region is between \u22122.23 and \u22122.48, for a spread of a little less than 0.25 dex in ionization parameter. If the points are on the low-metallicity branch, then they fall near but slightly below <em>Z</em>\u00a0=\u00a08.23 with very little spread. However, if they are on the high-metallicity branch, they fill the region <em>Z</em>\u00a0=\u00a08.23\u22128.53, with a spread of about 0.30 dex.</p><p>The O32\u2013Ne3O2 plane suggests that SGAS J1723 has a slightly higher ionization parameter than the O32\u2013R23 plane implies, with values falling between log<em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22121.98 and log<em>U</em>\u00a0= \u22122.23; the spread is similar, still about 0.25 dex. Again, the variation is almost entirely in the ionization parameter and is most apparent in the O32 dimension. Unlike the O32\u2013R23 grid, the Ne3O2\u2013R23 grid is not double-valued, and the Ne3O2 values suggest that the metallicity in every region of SGAS J1723 is somewhat higher than we inferred from the O32\u2013R23 grids. Still, if we assume that this means that SGAS J1723 falls on the high-metallicity branch in O32\u2013R23 space, then those metallicities agree with the Ne302\u2013R23 metallicities.</p><p>SGAS J2340 is quite different from SGAS J1723 in a number of ways. Of particular interest is the more extreme spatial variation. While regions A and B are very similar in both ionization and metallicity, region C is nothing like them. Both grids, O32 versus R23 and O32 versus Ne3O2, show that regions A and B, as well as the complete image, have ionization parameters that are tightly bunched about halfway between log<em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22122.73 and log<em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22122.98 (i.e., around log<em>U</em>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22122.85). This is not the case for region C, which has a much higher ionization parameter. While the lack of a robust detection in Ne3O2 diminishes its utility as an indicator of ionization parameter, the location of region C in the O32\u2013R23 plane suggests that it has an ionization parameter of either log<em>U</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a0\u22122.65 (low-metallicity branch) or \u22122.23 (high-metallicity branch). In the low-metallicity case, the offset between region C and the other regions in ionization parameter is about the same size as the spread in ionization parameters across the different regions of SGAS J1723. In the high-metallicity case, the offset may be more than twice as large. Unlike SGAS J1723, though, this variation is driven by a single unique region\u2014the rest of SGAS J2340 is nearly uniform in log<em>U</em>.</p><p>The interpretation of metallicity for SGAS J2340 is a little more difficult because some of the points, particularly in the O32\u2013R23 plane, fall outside the model grid. This is likely a real phenomenon, as these points lie in a region of the O32\u2013R32 plane that is populated by <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02 galaxies in MOSDEF (Reddy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib64\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib64\">2018</a>), <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02\u20133 galaxies in Nakajima et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib51\">2013</a>), and <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a03.3 galaxies in Onodera et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib55\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib55\">2016</a>). Why the models do not account for this is unclear, but there are several sources of uncertainty in the photoionization models that could lead to this. Nonuniform conditions within emission regions, uncertainties in the calibrations of strong line diagnostics, and uncertainties in atomic data all contribute to uncertainties in the location of grid points. If we assume that the points that fall off of the O32\u2013R23 grids for SGAS J2340 are actually at or near the grid's fold, then the metallicity is around <em>Z</em>\u00a0=\u00a08.23.</p><p>Small uncertainties in the Ne3O2 ratio correspond to large uncertainties in the inferred <em>Z</em> from the O32\u2013Ne3O2 grid. Still, that grid indicates that regions A and B and the complete image fall at relatively low <em>Z</em>, around 7.63\u20138.23; however, it does not rule out metallicities as high as 8.53. Region C, based on O32 versus R23, can be around <em>Z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07.7 if on the low-metallicity branch or \u223c8.8 if on the high-metallicity branch. Since region C has a higher ionization parameter than the other regions and is substantially less reddened, it would seem reasonable for it to be on the low-metallicity branch. However, we do not have an [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]/H<em>\u03b1</em> measurement for this region to break the degeneracy.</p><p>Overall, these two galaxies exhibit variation in ionization parameter of at least 0.25 dex. The metallicity variation is probably smaller, but the double-valued O32\u2013R23 grid makes it difficult to say definitively. The variations in ionization and metallicity in SGAS J1723 manifest as a slight variation across the different regions. Regions A and B are more similar to each other in all of log <em>U</em>, <em>Z</em>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn64.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=EVb75fiRdcuZKpoNhkz8VJvHGhM%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span>, and SFR than they are to regions C or D (which themselves are more like each other than they are like A or B). Because of the proximity of A to B and C to D, this looks like the physical conditions are, perhaps, spatially correlated, but they are not necessarily representative of a radial gradient (since the morphology is so clumpy and the variations are driven by differences in the clumps) and may simply be indicative of asymmetry. It is much clearer, though, that the variation in SGAS J2340 is driven almost entirely by one single spatial region (C) that is very different from the others, especially in log <em>U</em>, <em>Z</em>, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn65.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=5XqBIKCAoFB7KJLuqV2Dqttj3lM%3D\" alt=\"$E(B-V)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">E(B-V)</script></span></span>. This, too, appears more like an asymmetry than a radial gradient except in SFR. It is possible that these asymmetries are indicative of a recent or ongoing merger (e.g., region C being accreted by a galaxy composed of regions A and B).</p></div></div></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s6\" name=\"apjac0257s6\">6.\u00a0Discussion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>In the previous sections, we presented observational evidence for significant spatial variation in strong line ratios and the physical conditions that drive them across two galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.4. This finding has significant implications for interpreting current observations of field galaxies, as well as implications for planning future observations; here, we explore some of these potential impacts. We focus primarily on observable strong line ratios, rather than physical parameters like <em>U</em> and <em>Z</em>, because direct observables are model independent.</p><h3 id=\"apjac0257s6-1\" name=\"apjac0257s6-1\">6.1.\u00a0Reddening</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The finding that reddening can vary spatially across <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.4 galaxies should not be surprising, but it importantly affects the interpretation of other observed strong line ratios. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f7\">7</a> shows the H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> ratios for each spatially resolved region, compared to the ratios from the spatially integrated spectra. While there may be slight tension between the value for region B in SGAS J1723 and the value derived from the spectrum of the whole arc, there is relatively little variation in reddening throughout the regions visible in the giant arc, and no conflict with the line ratio measured from the spectrum of the complete image, despite the fact that it contains more of the underlying source galaxy than just the regions contained in the arc. This is not particularly surprising, though, since the part of the source that is not imaged in the arc is relatively small, with low surface brightness compared to the rest of the source. It is actually somewhat remarkable that the reddening in the individual regions agrees so well with the reddening of the arc and the complete image despite the spectra of the latter two being essentially wavelength-by-wavelength flux-weighted averages of the spectral properties of regions A\u2013D. This did not have to be the case, as shown clearly by the H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> ratios in SGAS J2340. The line ratio in the spectra of the complete images is much more representative of the bright, similarly reddened regions A and B than it is of the much fainter and much less reddened region C.</p><p>With this in mind, we explore the consequences of using spatially integrated reddening corrections to spatially resolved spectra, as one might want to do for higher-redshift targets where the H<em>\u03b1</em> line is shifted redward of the G141 grism. Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f11\">11</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f12\">12</a> show the difference between the measured values of R23, O32, and Ne3O2 with a spatially resolved reddening correction applied compared to what we would get using a global correction from either the complete images of SGAS J1723 or SGAS J2340 or the giant arc for SGAS J1723. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f11\">11</a> shows the impact on the reddening-corrected R23, O32, and Ne3O2 ratios. While individual values do not typically change by much, the slight excess in reddening observed in region B is enough to have an important effect on its O32 ratio. By not using spatially resolved values of H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em>, we would incorrectly infer that the value of O32 in region B is actually higher than in region A, even though this is not the case. While the overall difference is low (\u223c10% between using the spatially resolved reddening correction and the correction derived from the reddening of the complete image), this type of uncertainty could influence searches for spatial gradients in ionization parameter or metallicity. In SGAS J2340 (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f12\">12</a>), we see no such changes in ordering, but the value of O32 in region C is noticeably underestimated (\u223c30%) when not using the spatially resolved reddening correction. Since high O32 correlates with leakage of ionizing photons, searches for LyC leakers that depend on indirect indicators like O32 could miss candidates if they apply spatially integrated reddening corrections.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f11\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f11\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f11_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=xi0zYH%2F9K5S0uucH2Tavd9hLWNY%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 11.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 11.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f11_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=xi0zYH%2F9K5S0uucH2Tavd9hLWNY%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 11.</strong>\u00a0From top to bottom, R23, O32, and Ne3O2 of individual spatially resolved regions in SGAS J1723 color-coded by region. Each column of plots displays these values determined using different reddening corrections. Using a reddening correction derived from the spatially resolved spectra (left column) clearly influences the O32 value of region B and brings it below the value of region A, compared to using reddening corrections from the spectrum of the complete image (middle column), or the spectrum of the entire giant arc (right column). This demonstrates the potential importance of obtaining spatially resolved reddening indicators rather than assuming a single uniform reddening for an entire galaxy.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f11\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f11_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=xi0zYH%2F9K5S0uucH2Tavd9hLWNY%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f11\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f11_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=PYlpxvQ6axN2KHzulvmZvGEliEE%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f12\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f12\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f12_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=zM2%2F4VAlzhABSPuaFJaf6CJ1A3A%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 12.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 12.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f12_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=zM2%2F4VAlzhABSPuaFJaf6CJ1A3A%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 12.</strong>\u00a0Same as Figure <a href=\"#apjac0257f11\">11</a>, except for SGAS J2340.
