In this case there is no giant arc, so the left column uses spatially resolved H<em>\u03b1</em>-to-H<em>\u03b2</em> ratios to deredden the spectra, while the right column uses the ratio from the stack of the complete images. Once again, this has a noticeable impact on O32. In particular, O32 is higher in region C when spatially resolved reddening corrections are used. This is likely because its reddening is much lower than what would be inferred from the spectrum of the complete image as shown in Figure <a href=\"#apjac0257f7\">7</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f12\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f12_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=zM2%2F4VAlzhABSPuaFJaf6CJ1A3A%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f12\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f12_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=u0qdKH8Tgsl7NmKn2CEXLYRPuH0%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The fact that spatially resolved reddening corrections can have this kind of impact is a particularly important consideration for planning observations in the near term because there is only a small window of redshifts where the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 doublet and the H<em>\u03b1</em> line are both observable with space-based, spatially resolved spectroscopy at this point in time (<em>z</em> \u223c 1.15\u20131.58 with the HST WFC3/IR grisms). Without both of these features, one cannot determine a reddening-corrected value of the O32 diagnostic, for instance.</p><p>These two objects were chosen to fall within that window, but most potentially interesting targets will not. It may be tempting to extend this window by assuming spatially uniform reddening and using a spatially integrated H<em>\u03b1</em> measurement from ground-based spectroscopy, for example, to determine the reddening. Doing so would expand the observable redshift range to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02.4 by making the reddest line of interest the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007 doublet instead of H<em>\u03b1</em>. While this may work for sources like SGAS J1723 where the reddening is relatively uniform spatially, it could cause problems for sources like SGAS J2340 where there is significant variation in reddening. In fact, as we have seen here, even the relatively low variation in reddening within SGAS J1723 may be enough to meaningfully affect the interpretation of strong line ratios of a region like B.</p><p>When reddening cannot be measured in a spatially resolved way, it is likely that regions of higher extinction will be missing or underrepresented. This presumably also affects HST surveys that use broadband rest-frame UV light as a tracer of star formation, as well as H<em>\u03b1</em>-based surveys with the HST grisms. Currently, interpretation of spatially resolved HST grism spectroscopic studies of high-redshift galaxies is limited by the lack of H<em>\u03b1</em> sensitivity beyond redshift 1.58. This will be little changed by the grisms available on the Roman Space Telescope (H<em>\u03b1</em> will be detectable only to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.94). JWST's NIRISS grisms will extend the range where H<em>\u03b1</em> is available slightly, to 2.38. The NIRCam grisms on JWST will extend it much further, to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.61, capturing much of the available strong-lensing sample. However, the most progress will come from spectroscopy with the IFUs on JWST's NIRSPec and MIRI instruments, which will be able to measure spatially resolved H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em> ratios\u2014and better yet, Paschen-<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b1</em> ratios\u2014over a much larger range of redshift than is possible with the HST WFC3-IR grisms. Additionally, the IFUs will minimize the impact of contaminating light from members of the lensing cluster, which can be quite significant for the largest, most magnified arcs when using slitless spectroscopy; provide enhanced spatial resolution in arcs that are also magnified in the radial direction; and provide substantially higher spectral resolution, enabling splitting of important closely spaced lines like H<em>\u03b1</em> and the [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] doublet. These advantages, of course, will come at the cost of a smaller field of view than the HST grisms or the NIRCam and NIRISS grisms permit, requiring multiple pointings and mosaicking to cover an entire arc, so there will still be a role for slitless grism spectroscopy in studies like these.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s6-2\" name=\"apjac0257s6-2\">6.2.\u00a0O32, R23, Ne3O2</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We do not detect statistically significant spatial variation in Ne3O2. This is at least partly due to the fact that [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]\u00a0<em>\u03bb</em>3869 is difficult to disentangle from nearby lines at the low spectral resolution of the HST grisms. In addition, in the MAPPINGS models, while Ne3O2 is more sensitive to <em>Z</em> than to log<em>U</em>, small uncertainties in Ne3O2 can translate to large uncertainties in <em>Z</em>, such that it does not usefully constrain <em>Z</em>. R23, which does show significant spatial variation, more powerfully discriminates between different <em>Z</em> values than does Ne3O2. The downside is that the MAPPINGS grid is double-valued in the O32\u2013R23 plane, and the spectrographs with high spatial resolution at these wavelengths (WFC3-IR grisms) lack the spectral resolution to obtain other spatially resolved indicators to break the degeneracy. Ultimately, high spectral resolution, high spatial resolution spectroscopy of lensed galaxies is necessary to break the degeneracy by obtaining, for instance, a spatially resolved [N <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]/H<em>\u03b1</em> ratio. This will be firmly within the capabilities of JWST IFU spectroscopy, for instance (and indeed, SGAS J1723 will be observed as part of the JWST Early Release Science program, TEMPLATES; PI: Rigby).</p><p>We confidently detect spatial variation in the O32 and R23 ratios. By necessity, most of the spectroscopy of distant (<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a01) galaxies is spatially integrated, so we now compare the spatially integrated values of O32, R23, and Ne3O2 to the spatially resolved values to see what, if anything, we are missing in typical observations. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f8\">8</a> shows this comparison. There are clear differences in the results. The value of R23 measured from the complete image of SGAS J2340 is most in agreement with the value for region B. However, the values for regions A and C lie significantly higher and lower, respectively, than the value for the complete image. Meanwhile, even though the O32 value for the SGAS J2340 complete images is near the values for regions A and B, it is significantly below the value for region C.</p><p>SGAS J1723 further illustrates how spatially integrated spectra can obscure the actual physical conditions within a galaxy. While the O32 value for the complete image agrees with the values in regions A and B, it disagrees with the values for regions C and D and is only barely compatible with the value for the integrated spectrum of the entire giant arc. The value for the giant arc, interestingly, lies below the values for regions A and B but above the values for regions C and D. Even though there is general agreement between the spatially resolved and the spatially integrated values of R23, it is clear that, in general, the physical conditions in subregions are not necessarily well represented by the values inferred from spatially integrated spectra of either complete images or giant arcs. Just as studies of the stacked spectra of many galaxies miss the unique characteristics of individual galaxies, so too do the integrated spectra of single galaxies miss the unique characteristics of individual physical regions within them.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjac0257s6-3\" name=\"apjac0257s6-3\">6.3.\u00a0Implications for Finding Galaxies That Leak Ionizing Photons</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Galaxies with high O32 ratios are found to be leaking ionizing photons at much higher rates than the general galaxy population (e.g., Nakajima et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib51\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib51\">2013</a>; Izotov et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib30\">2018</a>). In particular, Izotov et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib30\">2018</a>) suggest that a flux ratio of [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727\u00a0\u2273\u00a05 is necessary but not sufficient for a galaxy to be leaking ionizing photons. (Note: while this is a ratio of [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] to [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], it is not the same definition that we have been using for O32 in this paper. See discussion in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjac0257s5-7-2\">5.7.2</a>.) In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f13\">13</a>, we plot this ratio (using their definition) for each of the regions in SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340, as well as for the spatially integrated spectra, to determine how using spatially integrated spectra would have influenced a search for LyC leakers that included SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. The [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727 and <em>\u03bb</em>3729 lines are not resolved in the grism spectra, so in order to assign a value of [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> ] <em>\u03bb</em>3727 to each region, the blended [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727+3729 values were multiplied by the spatially integrated <em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 ratio determined from the ground-based ESI data. For SGAS J1723, this is the value for the integrated spectrum of the giant arc. For SGAS J2340, this is the value for the summed integrated spectra of all four complete images.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f13\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f13\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f13_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=5dEuHW4LcvHMciDLwfqSvz3nfQg%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 13.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 13.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f13_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=5dEuHW4LcvHMciDLwfqSvz3nfQg%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 13.</strong>\u00a0A slightly different parameterization of the [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]-to-[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] ratio, this time [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727. This ratio has been suggested to be an indicator of possible LyC leakage if it exceeds 5 (dashed line). Since the spatially resolved grism spectra cannot spectrally resolve the <em>\u03bb</em>3727/<em>\u03bb</em>3729 doublet, the value of that ratio is set based on the ground-based spatially integrated ESI spectra (though based on Figures <a href=\"#apjac0257f7\">7</a> and <a href=\"#apjac0257f8\">8</a>, it is not necessarily good to assume that ratios like this do not vary spatially). While the spatially resolved spectra do not result in identifications of LyC leakers where the spatially integrated spectra did not for these two specific sources, SGAS J2340 in particular suggests that this may not always be the case.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f13\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f13_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=5dEuHW4LcvHMciDLwfqSvz3nfQg%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f13\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f13_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=DJWvdnSp4If%2B7jtb15sPVHdp6ks%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>In both cases, the spatially integrated O32 values lie on the same side of the threshold as the spatially resolved values. For SGAS J1723, all four regions have O32 values above 5, suggesting that they are strong candidates to be LyC leakers. The giant arc and complete image also yield similarly large values. However, the O32 values for regions C and D are somewhat lower than for regions A and B, and they drag down the value measured for the giant arc. So while SGAS J1723 would likely have remained on any list of LyC leaker candidates based on this criterion alone, it may have been given a lower priority for follow-up than it deserves, since region A is a stronger candidate for leakage than the spectrum of the sum of the giant arc would suggest.</p><p>SGAS J2340, while having no region that exceeds [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727\u00a0=\u00a05, still suggests that it is quite possible to miss a candidate by looking only at spatially unresolved spectra. The value for region C is much higher than what is implied by the complete image. And while it is still well below 5, it is not hard to imagine a similar case where the points are all shifted slightly upward and the complete image shows low [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007/[O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3727, but one small spatial region, like region C, lies above the threshold. If the physical processes that lead to the conditions that enable the escape of ionizing photons are spatially isolated events rather than large galaxy-wide phenomena, then surveys using spatially integrated spectra can be expected to systematically miss candidates with only one or a few leaking regions. In fact, it is already known that at least some objects exist where LyC leakage is a local, rather than galaxy-scale, event (e.g., Rivera-Thorsen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib66\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib66\">2019</a>), so this concern must be taken seriously as a potential source of bias.</p></div></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257s7\" name=\"apjac0257s7\">7.\u00a0Conclusions</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>To summarize, using spatially resolved grism spectroscopy of two highly magnified star-forming galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.33 and <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.42, we have explored the extent of spatial variation in observable strong diagnostic lines and the model-dependent physical parameters that they imply. We have also examined potential implications of such variation for interpreting existing data and for planning future observations, including with the JWST IFUs and the slitless spectroscopic instruments on HST, JWST, and the Roman Space Telescope. We summarize our main findings as follows:</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">There is statistically significant variation in strong line ratios like O32 and R23, but any variation in the Ne3O2 diagnostic is below the level that we can measure in these types of data.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">These variations lead to spreads of about 0.2\u20130.5 dex in metallicity and ionization parameter, depending on which metallicity branch these regions reside on in the R23\u2013O32 plane.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The Balmer decrement, H<em>\u03b1</em>/H<em>\u03b2</em>, varies significantly within a single source galaxy. Spatially integrated spectra yield values of this ratio (and of R23 and O32) that may differ substantially from that of individual, distinct physical regions within a single galaxy. Furthermore, applying spatially integrated reddening corrections to spatially resolved line fluxes can improperly influence the inferred values of other diagnostic ratios like R23 and O32.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">4.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The star formation in these sources is concentrated near the center of these galaxies, suggesting that they are perhaps undergoing inside-out star formation. Each source also displays a rather large degree of asymmetry in SFRs. For SGAS J1723 this is apparent even among the bright, star-forming clumps concentrated near the center of the source. The morphology of its star formation is perhaps more characterized by its clumpiness than a radial gradient. It is worth considering whether calculating azimuthally averaged gradients in properties like SFR is still an effective metric when applied to high-resolution data since asymmetries in annuli would make such a measurement quite misleading in a source like SGAS J1723. We suggest considering metrics like the clumpiness, asymmetry, or Gini coefficients of star formation instead of, or in addition to, gradients.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">5.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">If O32 is used as an indirect indicator of possible LyC leakage, then sources in which only a single or a few small regions are leaking LyC photons may systematically be undercounted in surveys that use spatially integrated spectra. Extreme O32 ratios in a single region, for example, can be drowned out by less extreme ratios in the rest of the source, causing a more moderate O32 value to be measured from the integrated spectrum.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">6.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">SGAS J1723, based on the O32 values in each of its spatial regions, is a candidate for LyC leakage. SGAS J2340 has less extreme ratios and is not as good of a candidate.</div></li></ul><p>\n         </p></div><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>This research was supported by an appointment to the NASA Postdoctoral Program at the Goddard Space Flight Center, administered by the Universities Space Research Association through a contract with NASA.</p><p>Based on observations made with the NASA/ESA Hubble Space Telescope, obtained from the Data Archive at the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under NASA contract NAS 5-26555. These observations are associated with program 14230.</p><p>Support for program 14230 was provided by NASA through a grant from the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under NASA contract NAS 5-26555.</p><p>Some of the data presented herein were obtained at the W. M. Keck Observatory, which is operated as a scientific partnership among the California Institute of Technology, the University of California, and the National Aeronautics and Space Administration. The Observatory was made possible by the generous financial support of the W. M. Keck Foundation. We acknowledge the very significant cultural role and reverence that the summit of Maunakea has always had within the indigenous Hawaiian community. We are most fortunate to have the opportunity to conduct observations from this sacred mountain.</p><p>Some of the observations reported here were obtained at the MMT Observatory, a joint facility of the University of Arizona and the Smithsonian Institution.</p><p>Some of the data presented herein were obtained at the Gemini Observatory, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under a cooperative agreement with the NSF on behalf of the Gemini partnership: the National Science Foundation (United States), the National Research Council (Canada), CONICYT (Chile), Ministerio de Ciencia, Tecnolog\u00eda e Innovaci\u00f3n Productiva (Argentina), and Minist\u00e9rio da Ci\u00eancia, Tecnologia e Inova\u00e7\u00e3o (Brazil).</p><p>We would also like to thank Glenn Kacprzack for his advice and assistance in the Keck ESI data reduction process.</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjac0257app1\" name=\"apjac0257app1\">Appendix: Stellar Mass Estimates</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Total stellar masses for each of these objects were determined using the MCMC-based (Foreman-Mackey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib21\">2013</a>) SPS and parameter inference code, Prospector (Johnson &amp; Leja <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib32\">2017</a>; Leja et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib44\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib44\">2017</a>; Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib33\">2019</a>), which is based on the Python-FSPS framework (Conroy &amp; Gunn <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib9\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib9\">2010</a>), with the MILES stellar spectral library (S\u00e1nchez-Bl\u00e1zquez et al.<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib67\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib67\">2006</a>; Falc\u00f3n-Barroso et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib20\">2011</a>) and the MIST set of isochrones (Paxton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib57\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib57\">2011</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib58\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib58\">2013</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib59\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib59\">2015</a>; Choi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib8\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib8\">2016</a>; Dotter <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib15\">2016</a>).</p><p>As input to this code, we used the demagnified magnitudes of each of these objects from the available HST and Spitzer bands. For SDSS\u00a0J1723+3411, we used the magnitudes of the giant arc, which required us to apply a correction to account for the fact that it is a merging set of two nearly (but not totally) complete images. For SDSS\u00a0J2340+2947 the photometry was summed across the three most magnified images, ignoring the less magnified counterimage (image 4) that is closer to the BCG and more contaminated by light from cluster galaxies. For each source, fluxes were corrected for Milky Way reddening.</p><p>We created detailed models for the light profiles of each of these objects using <tt>GALFIT</tt> (Peng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib60\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib60\">2002</a>) and calculated the photometry from these models. For the HST images, the models describe the lensed galaxies and the BCG, as well as any other cluster members or nearby foreground or background galaxies that may contaminate the light profiles of the lensed sources. PSFs were derived from the data directly, by summing appropriately isolated point-source images surrounding the model region. The initial model was constructed using a sum of the F390W and F814W (or F775W) images. This initial model was then propagated to individual HST filter images by re-optimizing it, allowing for small (\u223c20%) variations in fitted structural parameters in each step in wavelength away from the initial model, in addition to freely varying the magnitudes of the model components. Examples of these models are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f14\">14</a>. Total magnitudes of each lensed source were then derived by summing the flux across all relevant structural components that compose each image. Simple aperture photometry\u2014derived from HST images with the fitted central lens galaxy image removed\u2014is consistent with these more complex measurements.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f14\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f14\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f14_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=W8OMR4oVAzFUjFKPwqLDomp7a9Q%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 14.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 14.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f14_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=W8OMR4oVAzFUjFKPwqLDomp7a9Q%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 14.</strong>\u00a0Direct images, <tt>GALFIT</tt> models, and residuals for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. (a) The stack of the F390W and F775W images of SGAS J1723. (b) The <tt>GALFIT</tt> model of panel (a). (c) The difference (residual) of panels (a) and (b). (d) The F814W image of SGAS J2340. (e) The <tt>GALFIT</tt> model of panel (d). (f) The difference (residual) of panels (d) and (e).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f14\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f14_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=W8OMR4oVAzFUjFKPwqLDomp7a9Q%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f14\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f14_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=xjQt4h26PEcq5fQPhbeBOEGh8xY%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The Spitzer PSF has broad-enough wings that it was necessary to include additional model components to describe other nearby objects to enable a robust sky measurement in the modeling. The HST-derived model of the lensed sources is, in practice, more complex than necessary to describe them in the Spitzer data. In fits in which the source components are essentially unconstrained, it is thus typical that some components trend toward zero flux. Experiment shows that constrained fits, in which the components are all required to be significant, produce the same measurement in that the total flux summed across all the components that describe a given lensed image of the source is consistent.</p><p>Demagnified and Milky Way reddening-corrected magnitudes are tabulated for the SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340 in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjac0257t7\">7</a>. These magnitudes serve as constraints for the stellar population modeling. In these models for SGAS J2340 we assumed a parametric star formation history (simple tau model, with <em>e</em>-folding time <em>\u03c4</em> and star formation start time sf<sub>start</sub>, both in Gyr), dust attenuation applied to all light from the galaxy (in units of opacity at 5500 \u00c5), metallicity <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn66.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=otH7xxXuojtLHwShuc4SHjTb6Ac%3D\" alt=\"$\\mathrm{log}(Z/{Z}_{\\odot })$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathrm{log}(Z/{Z}_{\\odot })</script></span></span> (where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn67.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=In81ulKZj1mac228zP0Tcwn4Ftg%3D\" alt=\"${Z}_{\\odot }=0.0142$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{Z}_{\\odot }=0.0142</script></span></span>), and total mass formed in the galaxy (in <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn68.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=nBB%2B6GPX1iO67jzngyL%2FBIsbDJU%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>) as free parameters. The dust extinction and metallicity have priors covering the 2<em>\u03c3</em> range suggested by the available spectroscopy. For SGAS J1723, which was consistent with zero reddening, we used a dust-free model. These models each assumed a Kroupa initial mass function (Kroupa 2001) and that nebular continuum and line emission are present. We assumed the WMAP9 cosmology (Hinshaw et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjac0257bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjac0257bib28\">2013</a>) where necessary.</p><div align=\"center\">0.12</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small><p>\n                     <strong>Note.</strong> All values are demagnified. Uncertainties do not include the magnification uncertainty.</p></small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/916/1/50/suppdata/apjac0257t7_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ac0257\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257t7_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=yrqS3O6LgBz768tn0WDAz%2BjXmTE%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>As seen in the corner plots (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f15\">15</a>), the total mass parameter converges to a tailed Gaussian posterior distribution for these sources, which corresponds to model-generated remnant stellar mass distributions (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f16\">16</a>). The favored model for each of these sources is a recent burst of star formation, corroborated by strong emission features\u2014Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, H<em>\u03b1</em>, H<em>\u03b2</em>, H<em>\u03b3</em> H<em>\u03b4</em>, [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007\u2014throughout the best-fit model spectra (Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f17\">17</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f18\">18</a> for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340, respectively). As a loose check of realism, we compared the emission lines that are relatively unblended with others in the grism spectroscopy with the model predictions. We found that H<em>\u03b1</em>, H<em>\u03b2</em>, H<em>\u03b4</em>, [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007, [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>4960, [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] <em>\u03bb\u03bb</em>3727+3729, and [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3869 are typically somewhat weaker in the model spectra of SGAS J1723 compared to the real spectra (EWs 25%\u201380% of the real values). Model Balmer lines and the [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>3869 line for SGAS J2340 were somewhat stronger than the real ones (1.4\u20132.7<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a0the real values), while the values of the oxygen lines were in much closer agreement (around 75% of the real value). Of course, since nebular continuum and stellar continuum emission are much more important factors in determining stellar mass than nebular line emission is, modeling emission-line equivalent widths to within a factor of a few or better is sufficient for our purposes. Uncertainties on stellar mass due to an inability to precisely model the emission-line fluxes are captured in the posterior distribution of stellar masses and are relatively small compared to those arising from the magnification uncertainty.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f15\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f15\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f15_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=r2xNk6AOWCtRWmQnp5lQr5lFTTU%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 15.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; SF<sub>start</sub> is the time, in Gyr, at which star formation began. Vertical lines, from left to right, denote the 16th, 50th, and 84th percentiles.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f16\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f16_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=eJphfcjwqoXfFw7BML4aXq6FSOI%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f16\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f16_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=K97%2F%2FORxM04oAO75G7aQM31nYUo%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f17\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f17\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f17_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=mh7OxP2E%2BfK4tt94tVvUgRolD1I%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 17.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 17.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f17_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=mh7OxP2E%2BfK4tt94tVvUgRolD1I%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 17.</strong>\u00a0Top panel: the best-fit spectrum for SGAS J1723 is plotted here in blue. To visualize the spread in model predictions, 1000 other high-likelihood model spectra are plotted in gray. Photometry from HST and Spitzer data is plotted as red circles, with black error bars, while the photometry predicted by the best-fit model is plotted as black squares. For reference, the shapes of the transmission curves for the six HST filters and two Spitzer channels are plotted at the bottom. Middle: the residual (model minus observed photometry). Bottom: the <em>\u03c7</em>-value (residual divided by uncertainty) for each point.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f17\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f17_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=mh7OxP2E%2BfK4tt94tVvUgRolD1I%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f17\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f17_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=Z3pO2wBIxG5BA3slmgI9kE%2F5s0I%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f18\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f18\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f18_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=g%2FhbKVTzRzAD%2B%2BnuUbwbIwkxWbs%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 18.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 18.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f18_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=g%2FhbKVTzRzAD%2B%2BnuUbwbIwkxWbs%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 18.</strong>\u00a0The observed photometry, best-fit model spectrum, distribution of model spectra, residuals, and <em>\u03c7</em>-values for SGAS J2340. Colors and labels follow the same pattern as in Figure <a href=\"#apjac0257f17\">17</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f18\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f18_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=g%2FhbKVTzRzAD%2B%2BnuUbwbIwkxWbs%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f18\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f18_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=6o%2FbWwANtLRd8pBJuNI%2B6faIFVI%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>For SGAS J2340 the remnant stellar mass, based on SPS fitting to the six photometric data points from HST and Spitzer, is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn69.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=UHrHgBhiUPuj5Rh5UX9VojZe89M%3D\" alt=\"${9.6}_{-0.4}^{+0.7}\\times {10}^{8}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{9.6}_{-0.4}^{+0.7}\\times {10}^{8}</script></span></span> \n               <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn70.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=JFwhfA52ZSAnyTeIbn9okMjXK60%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>. The uncertainties used in the SPS fitting do not include the system-wide magnification uncertainty, which, when combined with the statistical uncertainties, yields a final mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn71.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=GeVuuQJ5%2FK1789ZZHbcY020CgIQ%3D\" alt=\"${9.7}_{-4.4}^{+9.0}\\times {10}^{8}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{9.7}_{-4.4}^{+9.0}\\times {10}^{8}</script></span></span> \n               <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn72.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=BAly3BJvA1GSHN%2BA%2FB268oEtcg4%3D\" alt=\"$\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>. We should note, however, that the models preferred a dust value slightly outside of the 2<em>\u03c3</em> constraint inferred from the Balmer decrement. Relaxing this constraint resulted in the model running to a slightly lower value of the dust2 parameter, but still yielding a stellar mass that agrees within 1<em>\u03c3</em> (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn73.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=RaIGfM%2FHAqHC5%2FW4LfIEyoVNMww%3D\" alt=\"${1.5}_{-0.7}^{+1.1}\\times {10}^{9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{1.5}_{-0.7}^{+1.1}\\times {10}^{9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>).</p><p>For SGAS J1723, the remnant stellar mass, based on eight photometric data points from HST and Spitzer for the giant arc, is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn74.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=mmk3QpWrd%2BJhJfvWoreiLbLDbl4%3D\" alt=\"${1.190}_{-0.371}^{+0.440}\\times {10}^{9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{1.190}_{-0.371}^{+0.440}\\times {10}^{9}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>. Because of the excellent constraints on the lens model of SGAS J1723, the uncertainties are dominated by statistical uncertainties in the SED fitting rather than by the magnification uncertainties. The arc, however, includes two nearly complete images of the source, so this value must be adjusted by about a factor of two. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f19\">19</a> shows the location of the caustic in the source reconstruction of images 1 through 4. Image 3 is a complete image, and the exact location of the caustic is better determined for it than for image 4, so we use image 3 to estimate the fraction of the source that is visible in the arc. To do this, we first drew a custom aperture around the source reconstruction of the stacked UVIS images of image 3. The UVIS data were chosen because the higher spatial resolution means that less flux will be spread across the critical curve by the wings of the PSF. We then modified that aperture so that it did not cross the caustic (i.e., so that it contained only the portion of the galaxy imaged in the arc; see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f19\">19</a>). A total of 95.7% of the flux contained in the original aperture is contained in the modified aperture, so the two images of the source galaxy that make up the giant arc are each about 95.7% complete. We therefore adjust the stellar mass estimate by 2\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a00.957, or a factor of 1.914. This results in a stellar mass estimate of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257ieqn75.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=noU%2FNj2l61SlLHWX2WvWByljgrI%3D\" alt=\"${5.95}_{-1.86}^{+2.2}\\times {10}^{8}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{5.95}_{-1.86}^{+2.2}\\times {10}^{8}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> for SGAS J1723.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjac0257f19\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjac0257f19\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f19_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=fXY%2F9A56xwftumbZVTBWv4gU4QQ%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 19.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 19.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f19_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=fXY%2F9A56xwftumbZVTBWv4gU4QQ%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 19.</strong>\u00a0Source reconstructions of four of the five images of SGAS J1723 labeled as they appear in Figure <a href=\"#apjac0257f1\">1</a>. Caustics are plotted in green. We used image 3 to compute the fraction of the source visible in images 1 and 2 in order to correct the stellar mass calculation. To do this, we divided the flux of the area below the green caustic and inside the cyan contour (i.e., the portion of the source visible in images 1 and 2) by the total flux within the entire cyan contour.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjac0257f19\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f19_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=fXY%2F9A56xwftumbZVTBWv4gU4QQ%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjac0257f19\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/916/1/50/revision1/apjac0257f19_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636904845&amp;Signature=gNeWhSbkVvQpSoxr2aDHjyBp7vk%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 The favored model for each of these sources is a recent burst of star formation, corroborated by strong emission features\u2014Ly<em>\u03b1</em>, H<em>\u03b1</em>, H<em>\u03b2</em>, H<em>\u03b3</em> H<em>\u03b4</em>, [O <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] <em>\u03bb</em>5007\u2014throughout the best-fit model spectra (Figures <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f17\">17</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjac0257f18\">18</a> for SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340, respectively). Columns (1) and (2) denote the source and the image or subregion. Column (3) contains the magnifications of each region and each complete image of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. Uncertainties are reported as the 68% level, e.g., for SGAS J1723 region A1, 68% of models that produce magnifications below 16.6 produce magnifications above 15.0 and 68% of models that produce magnifications larger than 16.6 produce magnifications below 17.1. Columns (4)-(10) contain the magnitudes of each region or complete image obtained from simple aperture photometry in each of the available HST filters using apertures that trace the segmentation map, with minor adjustments to divide up the individual regions as described in Section 5.3. For the purposes of planning future observations, the observed Hbeta flux is included for each component in Column (11), with its uncertainty in Column (12) (in units of 10^-17 erg s^-1 cm^-2). Rather than reporting line fluxes based on fits of individual, often low-S/N spectra, we report values measured from the stacked spectra of all images of each region, scaled based on the number of roll angles and the flux ratios from the broadband imaging. The flux ratios used for scaling here are determined from the stacks of the imaging data in the UVIS channel because the higher spatial resolution allows better separation of the subregions, while the flux ratios are consistent regardless of wavelength.\n", "Status": "Complete", "Action": "Scanned all subtables", "Table captions or footers": {"Overview": "Table 4 \nMagnifications, Magnitudes, and Hbeta Fluxes of Each of the Images and Subregions of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340", "Info after table 1": "Note. Columns (1) and (2) denote the source and the image or subregion. Column (3) contains the magnifications of each region and each complete image of SGAS J1723 and SGAS J2340. Uncertainties are reported as the 68% level, e.g., for SGAS J1723 region A1, 68% of models that produce magnifications below 16.6 produce magnifications above 15.0 and 68% of models that produce magnifications larger than 16.6 produce magnifications below 17.1. Columns (4)-(10) contain the magnitudes of each region or complete image obtained from simple aperture photometry in each of the available HST filters using apertures that trace the segmentation map, with minor adjustments to divide up the individual regions as described in Section 5.3. For the purposes of planning future observations, the observed Hbeta flux is included for each component in Column (11), with its uncertainty in Column (12) (in units of 10^-17 erg s^-1 cm^-2). Rather than reporting line fluxes based on fits of individual, often low-S/N spectra, we report values measured from the stacked spectra of all images of each region, scaled based on the number of roll angles and the flux ratios from the broadband imaging. The flux ratios used for scaling here are determined from the stacks of the imaging data in the UVIS channel because the higher spatial resolution allows better separation of the subregions, while the
